O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You dear children, I have completed this book which is the culmination of medical knowledge collection and compilation, finishing it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in my vision, I thought of completing it with this manual tool, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is highly practiced in our region and spread everywhere, if the science has been lost or abandoned, there are no longer any remnants from it other than small descriptions found in books written by the ancients that were used with the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and vanity have arisen, and closed minds occur, causing the loss of knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should renew this treatise together with the order of its content according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together in groups the forms of the metal cauterizing tools, and the other instruments of the operation with the adjustment of declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled physicians can be found in our times, the art of medicine has been lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	It is necessary that one who interferes in this matter become proficient in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as they understand the position of the limbs, their shapes and connections and separations, have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles, know the number of bones, the movement and location of mobile and stationary veins, and the origin of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, says Hippocrates that with a little effort you are much better off and with the use is slightly more so; similarly in the art of manual skill.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is unaware of the things already spoken about, they should avoid making errors and wasting others' time; just as I have seen many times with those who interfere in this science and abandon their knowledge and lack of experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	And I have seen a foolish healer who cut open one of the lymph nodes or neck of a woman and severed her neck arteries; because so much blood came out that the woman died in her doctor's hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another healer who treated a stone in an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to draw blood, and saw the arrangement of the body part and the size of the stone, and if he had let me cut him it would have led to his death.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw one other instance where I was called to treat another individual, the Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and along with the breakage there was an injury; and these clergymen full of ignorance would bend the break over the injury in many ways due to their strength, and did not allow any relief for the injury, and left him like that for one month; and I commanded him not to bend it again; and he remained like this until his leg was completely swollen and his feet turned, resulting in loss.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and bend the leg; and when I heard it bent so smoothly that he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was now confirmed in the member or body, and could not be cured; and the process of corruption continued within the member until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another mark that collapses an abscess, then inflames it due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a gangrene, when it is full of melancholic humours, it should not be touched with iron if it has not been cut in such a way that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because of this, dear children, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: meaning places where there are risks in multiple situations. And I will show each one in this book where it has danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you take care so that others do not speak ill of you. Take your weapons into account and treat your wounds lightly yet firmly, use the best way possible so that through the grace of God you come to health and remain safe; and leave unendurable diseases without complaint for cleanliness. Remove from yourself those who cause doubt about you, have faith in yourselves so that you can go from this world to glory with it.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen mentions in none of his admonishments: "Do not take any remedy for an illness that you might be called a foolish outsider.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medical water cauteries, and the chapters are organized from head to stone; and about the forms of tools, and the metals for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and the chapters are arranged and describe the forms of tools.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; and it is organized from head to stone, and describes the forms of tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remind ourselves of the work, it is fitting that I describe the quality of each remedy and its harm for each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I assert that the qualities of help and harm are the longest word and most subtle science and secrets. And many wise ones spoke about this, agreeing with it; they barely gave me their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I state that the fire cautery helps universally for all constitutions where there is matter, because it has two constitutions: this means hot constitution with substance and dry constitution with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the combination of hot and dry constitutions with matter, people proposed that the fire cautery is a great help; and others said the opposite: that the fire cautery only works for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is so hot, it should never be used to treat diseases caused by heat or dryness; and those who say the opposite argue that the fire cautery greatly helps with hot and dry illnesses that manifest in one's body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the condition of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true every time by experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And through all means, do not interfere with it except for the one who has experimented with it, and who knows by long use of medical knowledge, the art of cauterization, and the different complexities of human beings, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, as well as the occurrences and span of time; we have no fear from other complexities, even when dealing with cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them gathered together with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my children, that the assembly of a fire cautery has secrets in healing, and brings more benefit than a burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it only affects the limb that is being treated, not harming any other limbs if properly done.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The medicines that spread from one part of the body to another cause diseases due to cleanliness in healing; and by chance, the patient's illness is caused by fire because of its height and the goodness of its composition does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and through the length of my service and study in the art, based on truth of things; for which reason I excuse the length of speech, because it does not please me to reveal the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of work, how it relieves diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says when demonstrating this. Receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed on what times the cauterizations should be made, and set fire to them.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, for the injuries occurring are often mitigated by the aid of the cautery; and indeed, if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until the larger mischief does not affect the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like a fool, dear boy, as those who use cautery do; for sickness healed by cautery does not return. And they say it this way, but it is not quite so, because cautery is medicine that alters the complexion and dries out the fluids causing pain, being worth more than ordinary medicine due to its speed of action and virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the sickness comes at any time according to the complexion of the sick person and their condition of illness and its virtue; and in them, excesses are gathered by the intake of foods and similar things if cautery isn't administered in the place where there's a little excess and moisture, like hot cauteries for pain, and similar things, so this kind of pain doesn't return; but this happens seldom.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And few people understand why cautery is called the last of medicines; it's indeed to see. But they don't believe that cautery matches after medicine, but their understanding is false. Cautery is the last of medicines because when our methods for treatments fail in any sickness and they do not work, then we administer our cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it's clear that cauterization is part of medicine, not according to the thoughts of ignorant people though.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauterization instruments are more effective than those made of iron and they said this because of the quality of gold and its high substance; and they stated that burn marks from a cauterizing tool don't cause decay, but some people think otherwise as I have experimented with it and found evidence that supports their view in certain individuals; and gold cauterization tools are better than those made of iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	Yet still, when you heat gold instruments, you may not notice that they are heated by the color of the gold, and it is soon cooled down. If they are heated too much; if you put them to fire; thus, there's enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that is why we use iron cauterization tools that we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And you have ordered this chapter on the animal's head up to the nose, because its visibility is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	For the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive cautery is effective against moisture and cold in the brain, and there are two ways to do it due to an illness called 'soda', and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothaches, throat pain, and especially all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient's body is cleansed by dissolving medicine, transforming the head. Three or four times or five times, according to how the properties and the heat and the habit of the ailment can bear it; and then follow up on the head with treatment for the ailment.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have them sit cross-legged between your hands, and place their hands under the sides of their nose; after placing the base of your palm on the base of their nostril between their two eyes; and when your middle fingers reach that spot, if it bleeds from the inside, heat up the cautery called "olivare" which is in this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it under the line of ink, and move your hand down gradually while holding steady in twists; then lift your hand alone, and check if you see bone at a small solitary spot; if you don't see it, keep applying heat until you do see the bone as I have told you; after that take one pinch of ash, soak wet cotton lightly and place it under the line, let him be for three days; afterwards put on a moistened butter cloth; and leave it until the scab falls off; then treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they said to the old ones that when a wound remains open for longer, more pus is produced; and thus they were advised accordingly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burned, and then reset the one that has been burnt by the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the cautery must be left burning there, and press so hard that it removes as much bone wide as a little horn that women place in their bellies for when the fluids are expelled; and should we leave the wound open for a long time afterwards; then we must treat and stitch it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of using the cautery do not seem to me entirely good for everything; except in some people where there is a way of fear, and I believe that I should leave it like this. For the joints weaken by continuous discharge of nature, as we show with other limbs; even when the joints are weak due to nature themselves, and my first impression of using cautery is more healthy for me, and from these methods I take together a form of healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From old age pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain that lasts for a long time, one should use the patient's remedies of herbs and pills which are called "cochines", and treatments for the head and ears and bandages; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously mentioned to them, it proves effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take caution that the head of the patient is not too cold in nature; therefore, apply the cautery just under the one we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the cautery to each horn of the head up to the bone as we have said previously, do one more cautery on the side called "vassel", and insert one in that area where suction cups are used; and move your hand so you don't touch the bone: patients feel much greater pain in this type of cautery than in others, and I will discuss it further elsewhere. And it should be noted that the cauteries applied to the horns should be more precise than those applied to the middle part of the head, which is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	The fire cautery commands the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly in part of the head comes an acute pain, and the illness spreads until the eye, and the shoulder blade is purged by purgative medicines, and other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases have been done, and none of this helps: then make cauterizations according to two ways, namely with ague medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine-cauteries using ague medicine are as follows: you take a spoonful of ale and apply the peel and re-coatment over both shoulder blades, then place the temple in such a way that you can spread the spoonful of ale beneath the skin; when it has been spread, tie it firmly in this manner for 12 hours; then untie it and remove the garlic poultice, and leave the wound like this for two or three days. Then apply a poultice in butter until pus is discharged.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil cure as long as it is pure; and if you see that some of those burning medicines I have written about or in the tenth book of medicines that burn, you should perform.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery follows this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which I have described:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or has .i. pinch at the back, and midway there's a small appearance; and put it on the painful spot, hold your hand and gently move the iron slightly, until half of the thickness of the skin is burned; lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, when it exits, and allows an abundance of blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, place gauze soaked in salt water and keep it on the affected area for three days; then replace with cotton soaked in butter, and continue applying a healing oil as long as it remains pure. If you wish to cauterize this headache using the cautery called "cultellare", do so at its entire tip, but beware not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	Of the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraines as we have explained in the divisions of diseases before, and it doesn't help, and you observe that the cauterizations mentioned previously concerning medicine and iron do not benefit here, then it is necessary that you heat up the cauterization which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and do this such that your thumb spans half a span in length from the root of your limb, and hold with one hand once, and apply pressure so that you don't cut into the artery and only reach up to bone; and beware not to let any saliva interfere when eating, and have the nose focus solely on preventing it from closing like a snore, and be wary of bleeding in the artery if it is cut, or if one has great fear and likewise for those who are unaware and inexperienced; and leave the work halfway done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and show you where this happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you find that these cauterizations don't help with the illness and the patient is suffering, apply it in the middle of the head as we have said before, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see that this is not enough, administer the fire instrument that we mentioned or at the chapter on extracting the artery, using a fire tool with two blades; and know that these will be better than others and more effective.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold causes pain in the ear, and we have applied remedies that dissolve it as well as other treatments that we have mentioned in this division, and if the pain does not subside, then apply this cautery which is called "points", its use is as follows:

de la torture de la bouche	of the torment/pain in the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The treatment that should be cured by a cautery is not about those that move with urine, as we have stated in the divisions of diseases; and no cautery should be done on what seems to come from heat and nerve scarring.

Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there is the semblance of the sword injury which we placed before, but it is a bit more subtle; so it must be that the swords should be slightly thicker. After treating the wound as I said previously, until it becomes healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with apoplexy which is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and if the patients do not benefit, and the sick person has fever, then make these three cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, and one on the head itself, and one under the chin, and the last one over the mouth of the stomach; and follow this treatment as we had previously instructed.
de litargie	of liturgy

If it is done properly, well and good; if not, do this: apply three fire cauteries below the neck until reaching the collarbone, leaving an interval of one finger's width between each cautery. Proceed with treatment as usual. If you see it adjusting, and the patient suffers, apply another cautery in the middle. de la froidor dou chief	from cold of the head

de l’epilempsie	From the cautery
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine. Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize him, do by making points on all parts of the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the brain greatly; and then place a moistened cotton ball in butter and linseed oil.
de l’awe des eulz	regarding the treatment of eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun. And beware not to touch the artery so you don't cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "claw":

de coi ci est li forme:	of which I have described:

dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that touches the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time comes when the hair of the ears turns into wax, and it pinches the ear, and one performs cauterizations in two ways: namely by fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.

After cauterizing on the figure you have marked gradually and a little bit at a time, until the knees are burnt in that spot; and signs of health from the wound is that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs lifted to the tip of the ear; then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then apply moist cotton in butter until the scab comes off; after the ointment treatment until it becomes clean.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come, and the paper has been softened then begin the cautery on that same place as you did before; and when the hairs have fallen out, cauterize until the paper reaches its natural position, and is even, not touching any of the hairs.

The burning cauteries of medicine you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then shape the parchment as if it were a leaf of myrtle; take one part each of French soap and hot water and mix them thoroughly. Do this quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the form resembling a leaf of myrtle, and place it on the paper of the eyes; if the disease persists in one oil only, you should open it for one oil, and if in both equally; put cotton moistened with egg white under the eye. The patient's head should be covered with your clean hand while applying medicine, press once every time the patient feels a bite from the medicine because it also feels like heat.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the ablation is done, lift up his arm and reward him, if you see that the paper has been lifted as it would be by the constraint of fire or through incision; and if it is like this, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this doesn't work, try again with the medicine on your head or where the medicine hasn't taken effect, until all your actions are equal, and your eyes in good position; then place wet cotton in butter until the burned ears are covered, after treating the head from the ointment known as 'dyafenis' and others, until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if this requires that you keep well to your work by great care so that no medicine leaks into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes moist after that, and the hair sticks into the eye, then apply medicine to that part of your head which has become softened from clean paper in the same way as you did before; afterwards treat it until it is clean; and this is like the form of the mallow leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size and degree, and according to this, your instructions should vary; and do not prescribe for someone who has studied this art what is not appropriate for them.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy position; and guide the doctors to hold their head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or fall from its position; afterwards, apply moistened cotton on the inside of an egg or garlic juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery which is prepared: and place it above the head so that it forms like a feather pen; if you see it, let it be pointed between one part of the head to the other, and if you see it, let it resemble a tent; but always remember, whatever is placed above must serve for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it has been opened, and treat the putrefaction, then dry it; and if it is closed but still secretes pus, cut it out from the bowels; afterwards place a heated form on the cautery and hold your hand on top of the cautery at the part just below the ear near the eye, so that your hands do not cause mischief; and put the cautery in the oil grease, and let it become spoiled.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you proceed to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then redo the cautery one more time, and otherwise if you need it, leave it for three days. Afterwards, place damp cotton on butter, and apply the ointment healing salve until it heals properly, and once forty days have passed without proper healing, apply corrosive water medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow the recipe as detailed in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method for cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned.

des crevaices en levres	of cuts in lips

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess affects the root of the throat or in the lymph node, or under the tongue, or at the roots of the teeth, after it turns into a gangrenous infection and becomes discolored, hardening and forming a fistula; then you treat it as we have instructed in divisions, but if it doesn't heal, you must prepare according to your medical knowledge for what is needed. It's necessary that you have one cautery instrument suitable for the size of the fistula; after incision or cutting out the fistula, keep your hand until the cauterizing iron reaches the bottom and as far inside as possible; then perform this method once or twice. After treating it according to what we have said in treatments, while it remains healthy; if it heals like this, it's good; but if not, you must expose the wound and remove the rotten bone, depending on what you find when consulting your medical text.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that doesn't work, then put the head of the sick person in your healthy position; afterwards heat up the cautery which will come into play hereafter in this manner: you place a stick under the tooth; and place burning hot inside the cautery quickly, hold your hand until the diseased body feels heat reaching to the root of the tooth; after that lift your hand and continue with the cautery according to your desire; afterwards fill the diseased person's mouth with salty water, and let it sit for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the tooth which was moving is now fixed, and the softened gums are held back, and the moisture that caused damage becomes dried.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or frostbite, and medical treatments do not help, then it's necessary to use a cautery according to two methods: and the butter cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	The butter cautery works as you take butter from a cow, and with it the tip of a iron or spider's tool; after taking cotton and wrapping it on the point of a tent, and moisten the butter until it forms, then place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it cools down; and do this repeatedly until the remedy's effectiveness reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see moist wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on for as long as the fire reaches into the tooth pain.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cauteries should be such that you choose a rod of iron or bronze, and it should be large enough so that the flame doesn't reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, the form will come out like this afterwards, and place it on the tooth and keep your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be alleviated that day or the following.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it's necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, and then quickly rubs it in; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform the cautery according to how much you desire or are able to, and in this manner is it done for the application of a cauterization:
des scrophules	regarding the pock marks

Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:

dou cautere de pleuresin	A cautery of rue oil
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.
