After extracting the right tooth straight without breaking it, and if it doesn't spring back, take none of these instruments and insert them gently into each half, and move it like you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is torn and splintered, you should fill in the gaps with bandages at the point of the breakage; and if it's extracted subtly using tweezers, without causing it to shatter during extraction; and you must carefully open under the gum line for removing the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure to handle it well so you don't break it, and if any part remains, inform the patient of the greater pains caused by the remnants of the root after the initial extraction.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be cautious not to do as the ignorant surgeons do, who break the tooth in haste and by their boldness, without considering the instructions we've given; but instead, they often cause further damage from this disease by extracting parts of the root or tooth itself, just like we have shown many times. When the extraction is done, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding persists, which happens quite often, then you should fill the mouth with nitric acid solution; and if that doesn't work, apply cauterization.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments you first use should have long points and thick handles, ensuring they don't double when you pull the tooth; these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large limbs that do not bend while being used, and be made of strong iron well-crafted, with teeth for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the extraction, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with butter inside for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the nails are softened, and when you use the tongs called "algefri", which make the patient's nails look neatly trimmed; they should be done as if with a file and that is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out completely with these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh up to the root, and place the instrument known as "althali," which means palmache, as it is formed thus:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be hollow and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, that's good; if not, use all the tools you have, as their shapes follow after these descriptions:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if help is taken from this tool which has two points, as it is formed thus:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the size of teeth, and this tool which seems like large pliers, as it is formed thus:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be this instrument so it may not break, and know that few of the instruments of dentistry are; also other instruments which are not counted among them. And as such, skilled masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and diseases reveal to them, for there are some illnesses for which old teachers did not teach any instrument due to the variety within them and if any part breaks from the tooth or of another bone, or it rots, they look for the instruments that suit them, which I have mentioned, and help through gestures, as is this form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well designed to hold the bone, so that it doesn't escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore him with medicines suitable for this situation. If there is decay in the bone, and if it's small, when using this instrument take care of all these aspects:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not appear naturally and their form is ugly, especially in young girls where teeth are born after the first ones and cannot be pulled or filed: in such cases you must know that it's due to the teeth being born in a crooked position. Therefore, extraction is necessary; and if they are alongside another tooth, take this tool described here with this shape, similar to one small hook each, made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is ground slowly with my hands day by day due to the hardness of its root, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then I file it in a single piece like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it's also like the file used for making needles; and I grind the tooth slowly with my hands day by day gently, so that it doesn't move until it chips; then in the end level off everything completely with no sharp edges left, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must grind down the roughness until it's even, so as not to hurt the tongue or ruin speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is behind the jaw bone, through percussion or by pulling it outwards, and when the patient cannot press against what they are eating so that it does not cause pain, and you have treated with medicine that restricts it; if this is ineffective, it should be restrained by a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot but gold never changes. And choose a thread that is neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that one tooth needs pulling, take the thread and hold it in place between two healthy teeth, then insert the diseased tooth between any other teeth present, until you can feel the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering process up to where you interrupted, gently and skillfully tighten your hand, without causing any movement; and secure your ligature around the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the teeth with a thread on some pincers, and join them together, placing them between healthy tooth and tooth; and then keep it like that without hurting the tongue; and leave it like this as tight as it can stay in place, and if it dislocates or the threads break, tie it back with another thread; if stays properly and serves like this for all its time, and this is how teeth are aligned and the position of the two healthy teeth and the two missing ones appears just as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth are set back in their place, they should be reinserted gradually, as we have mentioned; do not interfere with anything that is not cautious and can tolerate it, and never shape them like an osseous tooth of a calf. Place them in the spot where the defect exists, and secure them as we have said, and let them stay and serve for as long as they can.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the threads come from beneath the tongue or its natural position when one is born; or by accident due to a healed wound. The procedures are as you work on the mouth for treatment, having your head in good health and keeping the tongue lifted. Then take hold of the nervous thread until the tongue has moved out of its place, and if there's stiffness or swelling, particularly from an abrupt wound healing process, remove the hook and cut the loose end. And make sure not to let the incision be too deep as it would go through the artery; when finished, lift the head up with a pinkish hue and slight coolness, then place over the tongue a linen cloth; and soothe your patients every night so that their tongues do not stick again.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding begins, set it with the iron tool on the wound; and if it doesn't stop bleeding, apply the slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat further until it has healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you notice anything that appears to be bloodied, black or hard, and your patient doesn't feel it, don't touch it as it could be gangrene; and should it start to turn into pus, and there is moisture, then use a hook to drain it and make a small incision from both sides, removing it from top and bottom; and if the pus remains in your body operation, place sulfur powder until it's healed, then continue with your operations as long as you have strength. Then lift the head with cool water and salt, and proceed with other treatments until complete healing occurs.
des apostemes de la gorge	From throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter comes within the throat valves which are called "godath", and they're properly named the II almonds. And when you treat them, as we've said in division, and if they haven't healed, then be careful: if these are tough, small-seeded abscesses of a hard color, don't touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it's red and the root is large, don't touch it with iron for bleeding; but leave it until it heals, then you will remove it, or it would burst on its own. And if it has a whitish color beneath and the root is fine, prepare your instrument to cover it, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, make the sick person sit in front of the sun, and his limbs be in their natural position. Let him open his mouth and have the surgeons press his tongue over the entire tool, as it is shown; and let there be a fine silver or thin iron like knives nearby.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue on all this instrument? And you see pus. Take the incision and put it in an almond, then pull it up more than you can; and don't remove any thing with, then shape it with your hands as it should be, which resembles some strength; and always both parts of head are corbed, and one part another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or fine tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, then shape it with pliers, which should resemble the form described above:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side and the other part of the name; and when you have done with one of the almonds, do the other in the same manner, and after making the cut gargle the patient with hot and cold water, or with water that is cool and mild. If bleeding occurs during this, then gargle the patient with hot water, or with cooked pieces of pomegranates, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then finish the treatment when it becomes healthy again. And do not let anything else grow in the throat other than the two almonds if you proceed thusly regarding them.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is the small abscess; and had successfully sealed off the entire throat, so much so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and could neither eat nor drink. She died if she had remained in this condition for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had required two drains each, at both nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurriedly performed the procedure and inserted an incision into one of his lungs. Then I removed that lung segment with a large piece of tissue attached to it. Next, I made another incision in the other lung's lower part near the diaphragm, then opened his mouth and pressed on his tongue. Afterwards, I reinserted the lung into its wound and took out some pus; only a little blood came out from that. Then he was released from his illness through this surgical procedure of removing the lung segment. He began to drink water immediately after that, followed by wine. I did not stop cutting into that wound for a long period of time. The wound was recovering right away and filled the place where I had removed the lung tissue completely until it became quite large again; then I cleaned him up and cauterized inside his throat. This way, he stopped getting worse and recovered. I left those places, and as far as I know from what God did after me, he healed perfectly.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it descends to the womb, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is large and spherical, it is called 'ovum'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure doesn't help, and you see that the extraction of pus has calmed down, and it's fine texture suggests you should take action; and for the one that is spherical and not long, and whether it's red or dusky or black, you need to avoid making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So when you see it, according to the method I have explained earlier regarding its size and length, you should make the patient face the sun. Then press their tongue onto the tool as described previously; after that, insert an ounce into the ovum and pull it outwards, then cut with the second instrument of the two I mentioned for incisions in the treatment of tumors.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not remove more than the surplus which is beyond the natural boundary; for if you take away too much, you harm the voice and speech. And after incision, use what we have said about incisions of the two mandibles, and treat it until the wound heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if they are in danger from excess, you should apply the instrument of cautery to remove them.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is done with an incision tool.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when the disease places its head in your health, then press the tongue onto the tool that we have said or the section on cautery, and rub it with a moist live coal, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this instrument, as shown:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place our head with a hair or where we apply the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the instrument with all of the medicine on the elbow; let the patient remain still on his side so that saliva and fluid from his mouth can be drawn by the medicine internally, without it descending into the throat or causing distress. Then hold your hand on top of the medicine and press it onto the elbow for about half an hour until you see it absorbed and the medication's effects are calmed; if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, soak it in the medicine, stick the tool with all the cotton into a wick from above, until the cotton dries on the elbow. Repeat this often until the cautery of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry, and clean after four or five days. If you need to restart the medicine cautery procedure, do so, and after that, use a cotton plug soaked in butter inside the elbow area, cleanse everything around the medicine; rinse with cold water and gargle until fully healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, nor than the cautery; if it's treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and myrrh and oregano and rue and chamomile and borage and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or any of these in one pot, and put it there, and bring it to a boil; and the pot must be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot place one tool stick according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether of silver or lead, and if it is one of the shoulder bones place in the mouth at the wound as long as vapor rises to the ovule through the canal, as long as the ovule is necrotic; after which you repeat often, until the ovule dries out, and ensure that you do not perform this method at the beginning of the abscess eruption, because many things occur; and do not use this method during the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a stick and place an eggshell inside the mouth of the patient so that the heat does not become too hot; because the eggshell does not allow the steam to accumulate in the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there's an opening in the bone or spine of a fish, with nothing else happening; so it would be suitable for you to extract what you can see and press your tongue at noonday on all the instrument, so that you can see movement happen; and that which doesn't open up inside the throat, then you should make the patient vomit as soon as possible so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it escapes through vomiting; or if the fish has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a bit of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it again; and when she comes back up to the top, if it smells good, and then proceed with extraction; and if it doesn't come out from what we have said, then take one tool of thong according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be directed towards the throat so that they can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head elevated up high; and guard not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing goes beyond it, nor push any bone inside; and move in such a way that the patient pushes the instrument, because if there is movement or if something becomes slippery; if she pushes the swallow, or pulls forcefully with all the instrument evenly, until she has the strength.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the substance of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the blood treated without (medicine), as I said in the division, through the administration of medicines; and if this does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, then press his tongue with the tool I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vessel, guide it with all your skill, or use delicate forceps that are suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't suffice, take a hairy stick and place it in the throat of the patient, then press where the hair of the stick bends, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you wash the patient with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full glasses of cold water, and work it in the mouth, then pour it down without letting them swallow, and move it around with their hands often; and as soon as the vessel senses the water, they will defecate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she doesn't defecate as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument we mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will come out without any disturbance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is as follows: you take a pot that contains charcoal and place it inside a screen in the middle. The head part of the instrument should be put into this screen. Then pour your fumigation, have the patient hold the tip of the needle in their mouth, seal the mouth so no smoke escapes but enters until it reaches the lungs; now the breath will come out, and if it doesn't, repeat the fumigation several times. Allow the patient thirst, consume salty things and similar items, do not drink water. Then it is necessary for her to expel this through that method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument to treat the discharge is like having hinged curved scissors for it to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a surgeon's hook, and it also has a roughness like that of a file, so whatever she takes, she cannot leave; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearance of pus discharges can be likened to what the memory brings forth from one and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and cutting; and there are two ways about it, one being in its likeness itself, and due to which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those who have them within their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those on the foundation, and the abscesses on the internal muscle are different from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses where one should not prick until the bowels are dead according to their completion; and for those that need to be pricked as soon as they are ripe, but do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are below joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come below joints, if you leave it ripe inside by chance, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes a contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For an abscess is in the main body member, and if you delay incision until it's dead, it will harm the principal body part. Or if it's beneath the foundation, if you puncture or do so even when it's dead; it should not be that you puncture an abscess without digestion completed, unless it is beneath the foundation in which case it might grow fully and be inside, causing a fistula; and cannot heal in a large manner.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary for you to know the time of abscess perforation that corresponds with maturation, and this is when the pain subsides, and the departure of fever, and reduction of pain and redness, and with the movement and hardening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; it is recommended that you have the perforation placed in the location below the abscess or at the point where it opens up, and also in line with the body length. The piercing should be made longitudinally along the body, whether the abscess is near hands or feet, joints and nerves, arteries, or any other place without a fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases when they bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are within the fatty part of the body, it is better to wait until you have completed digestion before making an incision as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you were to puncture before that, it would spread the poison of him throughout his body and be filled with many maggots; and by chance harden his skin and the parts beneath him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at no abscesses they puncture across the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you introduce small abscesses, small cuts; and in large ones, large cuts, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is customary to use a knife, and cover; when it has become as soft as cloth, and hardened, then you should do so like how one does with milk blisters: and for those that split into three angles, and those that are covered in the same way as the leaves of myrtle, like abscesses from angles; and for those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar cutting techniques.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it should be that you pierce them completely; and it is appropriate when the abscess is large, and has grown with great pus, and you pierce it, but do not drain all the pus in that moment, but only remove a part of it. Then let the abscess go until to another day, then leave nothing untouched; do this several times gradually, until all the pus has come out; likewise if the patient's strength is weak, or pregnant women, or young children, or aged and decrepit individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when he tries thrice with the release of the bow, that perhaps kills the patient, and you do not realize this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, if the wound appears, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a flat cut, use linen or old cotton bandages; and if it's a large abscess and there are many pus pockets, then you should stuff each one with a bandage so that they stick together; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and sewed it inward, then you should fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then set it, and dress it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood should start to pour out from your vein, cool it down with cold water and ease it off gradually, and hold the wet cloth there for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blood continues to flow persistently, then you should apply governance and treatment, using the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is due to an animal bite or an abscess, and if your vein or the area under the wound is very nervous, it is necessary for you to place wet cloths soaked with wine and oil on them; and if it is due to heat and the wound is reddened, it is necessary for you to apply wet cloths soaked with water and oil, or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the pus and clean it up according to what should be done, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this one should be known universally in treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the stomach
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the head region, small abscesses come about, and their manner is like those on cloths, similarly to a jeweler's work with a catkin, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and of such kinds with moisture as peas; and there are some that are hard like stones for the tailor, and there is no doubt that if it affects them, it will act contrary to this.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the scalpel is that you must prove it with every instrument which is called 'intermediary', from which the form comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make the cut above for its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape without leaving anything behind on the skin that contained the moisture, for it will return immediately if you leave nothing behind. Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound, letting it stay until the next day; and those who are healed by night come through this method.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And proceed to reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day and also on the third, until you are sure that it does not stay moist at night. Then dress the wound with ointment as appropriate, while it remains clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds on to be fatty, treat it in this manner, long ways; and cut your incisions, and burn all around, and put all your treatment of bleeding on the cloth where it is; and if the artery goes against you, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly handle the abscess if it is made of stone, and cut and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting on the stone-abscess and the wet one, it is lighter because they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or head or there is no moisture, and from these newer abscesses that I observed or head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and unable to break; and even if one had punctured none of them, it would have been treated equally well like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or head, it was the case that those which come from the heads of children and the roots of ears, the opening should be entirely free for as long as possible depending on the patient, in order to allow blood to drain; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	regarding the pock marks
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the throat, and close to the glands, and in the necks, and do not come to any other parts or on the body, they are hard, and are entangled with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly within its coat, as with the new and the abscess at the head, as we have said; and the appearance of these scabs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to submit to health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those where you see good arrangement on the pillow, and it has a color similar to that of blood, is mute from each side and not pierced through the neck or artery nor in the ducts; so it must be handled by placing over them, and cauterized from each part, and elongate both ears at the nostrils if necessary, as we have said about abscesses on the head; and handle it little by little, and be sure not to touch the nerve or vein, nor cut too deeply that the sputum does not spill out, and do not go ahead too much that you don't remove what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to open it, then insert powdered vitriol or any powders that release blood in the wound, and restrain the wound; and leave it like this until the abscess is appeased, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the skin is covered with blood, return to your work until you complete it. Then seek out your skill's indicator if there remain any small pustules, if you cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the pustule, it should not be that you cut the pustule at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall out through it without harm; then apply an old cotton pad soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you are dealing with all of the ulceration, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound, and now suture them, because there should be no excess remaining due to the size of the ulcer.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to cut into it, drain the pus, and suture it, just as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those ulcers that have excess, cut where it is open; and cut in the same way as previously described, from top to bottom. Then treat with ointments and similar things until they get infected by the corruption of what's already there; and when the wound has been thoroughly cleaned, apply ointment until the flesh grows back completely, so long as it heals properly.
de squinance	"De squinance" translates to "on squinting" or "concerning squint". This term could be referring to medical treatments or observations related to eye disorders where one eye may be turned inward (intorsion) or outward (extorsion). The specifics would depend on the broader context of the text that this phrase is found in.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones told and spoke of the surgery to cut the throat; but I never saw anyone perform this in our land, it's written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as 'the epiglottis' be made; and one should not attempt this by oneself, because all the veins and the lung are connected to those who have an abscess either in their mouth or in the throat or between two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis in order to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	So, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make cuts through three circles or four small slits across, between the two circles where the slit extends in proportion to the size of the slit, not into the cartilage. This allows for the cutting of the epiglottis without leaving any flesh and ensures that the blood vessels are well distanced from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat to all the inchin, then cut into the keur until it reaches the cheneil; and avoid any blood vessels, should you see anything, and then close off the syphle, just as we have said; and this can be demonstrated through the section of the fluid flow of the cheneil which jumps forth from the side that is broken, and through lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed in which one doubts strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound neatly, and all along the skin up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that create flesh until it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albacus suggests that one should not perform this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged dead, and the deficiency has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then stitch the epiglottis because the disease cannot leave, and he breathes through the wound, so you are spared from death; and for that reason, the old ones commanded to keep the wound open until the illness of the sickness passes, and it has passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and cleanse it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the windpipe. And I was called to treat her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and it was well that she did not have a cut vein or artery but rather the wind flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurriedly treated the wound and cured her until she was healed. And it turned out that all that the maiden needed was for her voice to be hoarse, then she returned to her usual self; thus I say that in the surgery of removing the epiglottis, one should not fear.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts called "throat hernia" are known as large abscesses of a deep chestnut color, and they occur frequently in women. They can happen in two ways: naturally or by accident; natural ones do not have any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidents happen in two ways. One resembles having fat inside us, and the other way resembles an abscess coming from our artery. There is fear involved, and it's not appropriate to open with fire except when the condition is small; prove this method thoroughly for all types: if you find that it matches exactly like fat we have, cannot reach any vein, then cut it out just like how we would remove fat, and remove everything cleanly, if there's nothing left. Thoroughly search again, treat according to need until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are there, from which I will mention all similarities; now it is fitting that I explain the entire difference between us and issues.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I state that dislocation is characterized by fever and heat persisting until the emissions have passed, and then completed decomposition; therefore, the fever and heat should subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new (condition), there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is along the color of body tissue, and begins in a way like a boil, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, oily or moist, and much of the color is as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new injury, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called 'intermediary', according to whether their shape appears or after chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of extracting pus from us is that you squeeze it more moist than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs a bit by a bit, until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the central material, and be careful not to rupture.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture is involved, regardless of what color it may be, if it causes it to split in the way I have described for other abscesses; and if after the incision no more moisture comes out, you know that it was greasy, then cut right across, and take hold with forceps, and gently scrape off from each side, and cover the wound where it is, so that you can take out the object clean. And if you cannot take it out cleanly, remove it piece by piece until there's nothing left to stay behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is nothing left behind, it will come out again many times; and if there's a little bit that stays in place without causing any harm, then fill the wound with corrosive powders, keep the wound clean, apply antiseptic dressings to the abscesses, and treat it with other remedies until it heals completely; and if the pus is large, you should cut both edges of the wound open, and treat the one that discharges pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or otherwise opposed and you hasten it, hold the site of the cut with vinegar powder, and let it rest for two days or three days, as long as the wound heals, then resume copper treatment that has been in use for a new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	This text describes the forms of surgical instruments used in operations and mentions three types: large, medium-sized, and small. There are also three different sizes referred to as 'albaret' or 'breb', respectively, for each type. These sizes allow for the proper treatment of fistula abscesses by encircling them effectively. The instruments resemble needles used in sewing clothes and can be made from citrine quartz, iron, or silver. The yellow-colored ones are said to work better than black tar in enclosing the deformities of the fistula. Lastly, there are three sizes for these: large, medium, and small, depending on the width of the incisions.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of scalpels resemble these: large, medium, and small. There are also scalpel blades that have two curves in three different ways, those with three curves and they too come in three forms, those having two curves and there are ones with just one curve as well, each again coming in three forms. All these are necessary according to their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this one they make to be sharp-cutting, and among such ones who do not cut power but from one side only, these they sear their limbs; because in this way they do not cut the vein nor nerve; and as for these introducers, their tools are held by hands, so that the patient does not sense it during abscess opening; and there are three ways: large, small, and medium, just as you see; and none of them use power but only in flesh cutting parts like legs, arms, nipples, at angles, and similarly on these; and no other tool is made too small that resembles surgical tools, according to this shape, with which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it should never be placed at the site of a healthy artery or veins, and under no circumstances follow this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the men's breasts swell when they start to be corrupted, until they look like breasts of women; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who want to cure them should proceed according to this form of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then remove the fat and apply medicine to treat the wound, afterwards stitch together the two edges of the wound and continue the treatment until it heals. If the nipple is tilted downwards due to its size as in women's cases, cut it into two parts above by two similar slits; one should stay connected to another after each slit at the end of both, ensuring that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up until the line .g.; then burn off the skin between the two edges and remove the fat, applying what we have said about stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for treatment until it heals; if not healed or when the incision isn't fully complete due to the inability of the flesh to rest or from blood clotting, fill in the wound with gauze soaked in corrosive ointment and leave it until it diminishes with the removal of the gauze and fat. Then continue treating until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses from the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Wounds that come from abscesses are manners of hard scrophules where there are nodes, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, you should fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply ointment until it heals.
