And if the abscesses resemble scrophules, cut them as we have said in cuts on scrophules, and if the wound is full of pus, apply a cautery as we have said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is injured and the skin is sutured above it, many times abscesses occur, and this happens similarly with veins and abscesses; and if one knows that it's due to the artery, then the abscesses are long outwardly; and when you touch it with your fingers, you sense a hardening; and when it's due to the vein, pus is evident coming out; and it's foolishness to treat this abscess, and similarly when it's below joints and bones in various other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one should avoid iron treatment. With respect to the one at the head, one should also avoid this method. If it's about an artery inflamed, cut through the skin as long as needed; then proceed with surgery using inches and separate the artery from the tissues as much as possible; then insert a probe under the skin up to the other side of the body, and stitch the artery by a double thread on both sides, following what I have taught you in extracting two arteries that are in temples; then pull the thread through between the two lines using an introducer until all the pus is released and cut off the abscess. Then apply the cure that follows, until it stops bleeding. And if the pus is due to the vein, one should dye your hand with a little of the pus on all the skin, then insert a needle under the line held in your hand, pierce it through, and attach another double thread, so you can pull from the other side; then tie off the abscess as I have said before, or bind one part of two arteries by a thread; and if you doubt whether the thread will release force, insert another needle under all the pus at the first incision point, and secure the threads in four places. Then cut off the superfluous pus, then cut off with the knife and leave what is tied. Then place a wet cloth on one side with wine and oil, then apply treatments of bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	The removals of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, when an abscess forms in the artery and vein, abscesses also form on nerves when they are cut, or due to excessive labor, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often with shoulders and elbows and in all places that have joints, it is the concern of abscesses, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is found in many positions without pain; and when it's constrained forcefully, the patient feels pain, and is not merely inside like from flesh but below to the neck; and moves well everywhere, neither going forward nor backward, neither downward nor upward, and one who is in joints should not cover with iron: by chance a contraction would occur; and that which is on head or forehead makes the skin go numb.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, and you have some tweezers, grasp it at its root; and if they are large, hold them until the elbow, then cut, then remove the scabs, then unite the wound to the seam, and the treatment until it becomes healed.
des grosses boces pendans	And for the larger blisters, hang them.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	No part of this text ever occurs in the womb or anywhere else; it's a disease called "fungus" by its appearance and has a subtle root, and large lumps; and there are also small ones and some that are quite large. And I knew a person who had two bellies which resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white and had small roots, they split open and immediately rotted due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I found them and weighed one at eighteen ounces and the other at six, and in the incision when you look it's that the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist with a subtle root; if you check it in spatumile large ones, and they are under your presence then use fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For the surgeon often encounters many times excessive blood losses during surgery, and if they cannot withstand this, then you must hurry with the cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful from the incision of the iron, take a properly made plonc thread and bind it around in such a way as we have said before, and leave it for two days; and then rebind it, not stopping to pull the plonc thread until the bandage copes with the binding, and it feels no trouble; and if the roots are large, they fear even in coping towards the belly, but you can well cope half of it, then cauterize so that it does not bleed again; then treat the wound and ensure that you do not over-tie the thread which is white in color and with a poor feeling and milk appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess that's been incised, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil burns
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	The appearance of the burn comes from the burn wound or cut in the bladder and is on the belly; there are some in the bowel; as it occurs in other perforations, or blood that escapes through veins or arteries according to what precedes, or due to windiness; and if this is by the perforation of the bladder and by the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of flesh, and is a light matter without pain, opening from different exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers it returns, and then comes back again, and by chance it might swell, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it's a light matter and opens well when you press it with your hand, not constraining; and if it's due to blood, it opens through these signs - the abscesses are large and hard, and lie according to their quantity; and if it's due to windiness, there is swelling at the touch, and in the work you should look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of an artery or vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary for you to allow the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear involved, as I have told you or in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.

des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or corruption is assembled there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, do so with all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and it has this form:

de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have spoken of the methods for stone division and extraction together with remedies; and we mentioned the difference between the kidney stones that float and all the signs, and on which stone one should operate by size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder occurs more often among children, and this is a sign that the urinary tract infection behaves like an inflammation in its subtlety; one should open the urethra, and massage the patient's penis several times, and then try to insert something; and many of these infections involve the foundation; and it's easier for small children to recover until they are four years old, it causes more distress in older individuals, and it is at a middle age for those between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those with large stones than for those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by purging, in order to extract all the pus that is inside.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it clogs up every time when trying to cut into the stone.

Then take the patient by the feet, and lift them up and move back so that the stone descends towards the bladder, and exits no longer from above him; then have him sit between your hands, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is fully hanging downwards; then look inside and touch it. If you feel the stone in space, cut now onto the stone immediately.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it doesn't pass at all during the touch test, moisten your left hand's index finger with grease of the palm side, for if the patient is female; or your middle finger if male, as this indicates a smaller stone. Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they place between what's in the kidneys and the base, not midway but at the edge of the left snowflake; and be straight on the stone, and let your elbows touch or rest on the base, and have them fit through if it's wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too big; by chance squeeze the elbow that rests on the base, so that she jumps out without effort; and know that there is a part of the stone where there are angles and edges: if it gets stuck; and in some parts, shaped like a walnut, round, from which the exit is easy.

dou chastrement	of chastity

Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	So I say that penalties are done in two ways: either by attraction or through a breach.

de erratique	Concerning the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic menstruation occurs when the nature of the woman is not fully perceived, or if the uterus is small; it is naturally determined by birth, or accidents caused by illness that has come upon her; or it's due to sexual excesses, or subtle or coarse fluids, and it manifests throughout the belly, or in the ribs, or underneath, wherever it may be. And one must understand how this happens, during childbirth, and occasionally while having flowers (referring to menstruation). And knowing these things comes through observing the appearance of the woman.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the strikes are closely visible, one should look at your hands or on the road.

Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if it's firm and dense, then you must shape its surface as it appears to be when resembling the leaf of a myrtle.

Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an embedded abscess in the wound, one should not apply fire to it.
des emorroides	Regarding hemorrhoids

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, because that part of the body doesn't have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I was to look at the wound and with my hands on its bones as far as the woman could endure; and I kept her long in this position, and so there was a little blood coming from it. And I have remembered this chapter only for when, if the masters find an unfamiliar thing, they should know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Following this comes the form of the applicator, to which the books refer; and in it are two parts for each of four limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In short, the horns should be finer than that of the restrictor and made of ebony or boxwood. The mouth should have a width equal to half the diameter of the shaft, and the edge of the teeth must match it, being one and a half palms long; and in between the two points, there should be two attachments of the same material as the shaft, which should be firmly attached on both sides, either halfway or slightly longer. These two attachments are placed in the mouth of the vagina so that they open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, can be made of ebony or buckthorn wood according to the shape of tongs; it includes two handles attached at a joint, as you can see here, one palm length long and one width wide. And when you observe the opening fully with all the instrument parts, have the woman lie down on the table, her legs hanging and her feet apart, then place both attachments together into the joint of the marris (possible medical term for a bone or joint), hold the head of the instrument between her armpits; then move your hand along the entire instrument as you would with tongs equally, according to the amount you can see opening the mouth of the marris. Do this until she achieves what she desires.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	All these instruments are mounted and multiplied in various forms; and when you have them set up, the work proceeds more quickly, and you can use them higher up for their respective sizes.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Don't lose hope in the tool if you haven't set it up, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage of childbirth is being held back by the mother, it's necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze with consideration. If this doesn't work, then take Ipot (pot marjoram), and make a poultice or cover, and put in the pot herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia leaf and comfrey; any of these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or steeped in water on fire; then place a reed or poultice over the pot's opening, and the other end of the pot is placed in the mouth of the marrow, and let it lie until the vapors emerge inside the marrow; then make them sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second tooth springs up quickly.

And if the mouth of the mare is too tight, we have said the cure for sneezing and herb fumigation; and if she does not respond to all that we have said, then be careful you do not force the milking; but it should be that whoever is at the mouth of the mare ties her to the woman's womb, then anoints her with tetraform medicine; she will expel and return powerfully; but nonetheless, when she does so if there comes a bad smell to stomach and head, and irritates the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So, it is necessary then for such treatments: none of the old remedies have proved that fumigation with sowthorn and dried figs works.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate a woman during retention of flowers and the second stage is as follows:

de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Newborns come forth who lack the piercing foundation, instead have been stunned by a subtle poison: henceforth for the sake of the cure, she should puncture that poison at its proper spot, and not pierce it with an excessively sharp tool, and guard the placement so as not to touch it; then apply moistened wool in wine and oil, then the ointment treatment until it is healed.

de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from the foundation are swelling, and those that come from deeper in, or in the space between two parts, if it's one fistula or multiple; and when this swelling is old, if it's active, and has accumulated moisture turning white or opaque matter, and any of these fistulas are palpable; and they can be recognized by whether there is expulsion or gustation when the patient defecates, and sometimes a sensation moving towards it.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if to fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and extend up to the knee joint, and up to the root of the testicles.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the sinus persisting at the foundation, and not persisting: and it is that you bend your index finger or foundation, and insert a subtle needle like a spider's leg or iron into the sinus when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, should you stick in a subtle tentacle like a manta ray or a horse's tail, as long as you feel the tentacle or hair on your tool; and if you don't feel it, and no pus, wind, or worms come out, as we have said: know that it has not pierced yet; so hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is almost through to the bladder or where urine flows, if it jumps with urine, and cannot be united by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it has pierced up to the knuckle joint, that's as far as the tentacle goes; if there is no twisting and internal pain, then it's inside, and it doesn't benefit from medicine or immediate ointment application; and for these persistent sinuses, there is no cure but labor and vanity of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In this that is neither Persian nor ancient, there's the hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it's that the wounds lie between your hands on their back; then lift their legs up to their thighs, and keep their thighs inclined towards their belly; afterwards place a spider's web tent, or if tortuosity exists in this area, continue until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the wounds are inside the foundation, it is necessary for you to place your index finger on it, then when you feel that the tentacle has penetrated; and discover where you can sense between your fingers the fat or the sinew, then you will know that it's Persian; if there's no movement at all, one can't heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can still manage to heal some cases completely, but this happens very rarely; and when the help is given, it's that we heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as previously described; then you apply it thoroughly into the fistula until it goes beyond the foundation; do this procedure two or three times, until you're sure that all those fatty remnants have been burned down, which resemble a feather of an oiseau; and then treat with greasy moistened tents until they are completely gone, then apply healing balm to the area where the fat used to be and seal it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it's so high, no other way can make him healthy. Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it doesn't satisfy you, and there's a gap between you and the operation, then apply a fire cautery or an ointment with medicinal properties.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauteries include two good things: that is, the burning of these fatty substances in their position, and the bleeding off of blood and the drying out of moisture; then treat damp tents that are greasy or ground-up into a powder, until the fat becomes liquid, and goes out through this burned fat; then heal wounds with dry medications which stick to hard flesh, and they become dried medicines.

If you feel the tent (possibly referring to a surgical procedure), and it is in the place of the suture or stitch where it's about to puncture, if there's no other way out than a vein or artery, then by administering one of the three methods: or you sear it as we have said, or you remove until you hit bone, or if you can remove and cure it like the first; don't go too far in your procedure that you cut into the structure holding the foundation, allowing for voluntary ejections; then proceed to treat by cleaning, just as we've said; perhaps after this they recover. Or you remove that covering and clean it thoroughly once it's been cut off from below the foundation, or through trial or another pointed instrument; then cleanse that newly formed scar in the wound area as much as possible; then study how to heal the wound and manage the fistula in the part beneath the foundation: if this is a lighter issue for the patient.

If it is Persian in the fold beneath the foundation within, then extract that thread of the torn one, just as you puncture its base or foundation; and pull out the head with the thread, and assemble the two edges together, and hold them together, and let them be for one or two days; and hold it no more times until the threads join those parts that are between two, and become fused; then treat the wound until it is healed and cleansed.
