Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spineous spathile from which one makes an incision is many and varied, either cutting; and on another side no, because we do not join what we should not, as you see here:
des emorroydes	From hemorrhages
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Wounds occur in two ways: either they are within the foundation, like a seed of resin, and if there are small and large ones, and they fill the cavity with blood, and if there is one or more, and are outside the foundation and close to the edge of it; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still contain a little yellow water or some blood, and have the color of skin; and the treatment for these that have them within the foundation, you should instruct the patient to bleed in chambers until the foundations come out and they can be seen by their filaments; if you hurry, and hold it with tongs, or keep it with your finger, then cut at its roots. And if the seed cannot hold because of its moisture, take them with a sponge, or on cotton, or from camel wool; and remove them with your hands, then cut them, and apply heated powders that are equivalent to cautery; you should cauterize them as it is said in the chapter about cautery, and treat with other treatments until they heal. And if the foundations cannot come out, you must force the patient into a purging by having them take bitter and sharp purgatives to wash what is inside the foundation, so that it may be able to come out completely; until the patient has improved, and when his filaments are strong in relation to the foundation, then this treatment will be mild; and you should pinch them with your fingers or tongs, cut them, and treat them as we have said until they heal and fear surgical incision.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you stitch according to this manner: take a twisted thread and place it in a needle and then pull the thread upwards, cause the needle to pierce from another side, then loop twice over the thread on the needle and do so evenly; and firmly hold the thread, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and repeat for all others. And leave some for the excess bleeding; then place an oily cloth or ointment on the wound bed and apply it, then place another bandage on top of this. Instruct the patient to rest; and let them lie until they have healed completely, when they are settled in their health, then treat with ointment and other treatments, until they recover fully.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	do drying by sweat or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it causes bowel dryness within the intestines, and due to natural constraints, and when the illness is old and medicine no longer works.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the tip of a spatumile or above your nail's edge, which should not remain moist. Then treat until it hardens as it should; and if it does not harden, re-shave more forcefully than before, until it heals somewhat and becomes scoured; then treat until it has fully healed.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A small trace appears before the body, and goes completely forward; and whenever the pulse is taken it cools down, and one can also feel it like a death tremor, and comes throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take one of goose feather or a powerful vulture's feather, and place this stick on the tremor until the purplish circles encompass entirely the tremor. Then move your hand with all the stick until you cover entirely the tremor, and place it forward, thus uprooting the tremor from its source.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do as follows with a spider's hair or iron according to this shape, and let it be slender underneath and sharp above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't pierce it, but hold it between your fingers and squeeze it firmly. If you see this, apply the cautery to the tremble, as depicted in front or chapter of the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the shape of the bladder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a bladder of silver or tinplate, or iron melted down or lead; and never make these tools big or small, according to how they are ordered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those thus take on the task of healing children and those who are weak and painful, being little.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bladder is small at the top and large, or the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I'll tell you about when the stomach seems to be twisted, as if you can see it, and is pierced inside; there's two holes on one side and one on the other; then place your medicine in a beast bladder or parchment near where the stomach is, pierce thoroughly with small needles, leaving an inch of space between each needle. Then insert into these needles a strong thread twisted in an X or zigzag pattern, sew the stomach like a sheep would be stitched; once the medicine's inside, attach it to the tool before with a thick thread, then you'll enemas this medicine out and that will create the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And make sure the medicine is neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or yolk of egg balm or something similar, then gently rub it in. Then direct the attendants to use both hands together on him until he can see everything clearly; then remove the cyst, and raise the patient's legs at the edge of bed, if the medicine is meant to come out, do so as much as possible; and if they sleep all night through, that is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use it to treat illness characterized by the loosening of abdominal contents, and the medicine seeks to quickly emerge, then continue using it as long as it is effective.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bleeding from the root or base of a wound, or an abscess, even if the cyst is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle cyst under which the skin is constricted:
des plaies	from wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have discussed the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will talk about hand treatments and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and where on the body they occur, and why they have occurred.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The causes of wounds are due to penetration by stones, the size of a sword and knife or a lance or shaft or dart, or similar things; they can be done according to the parts of the body like a wound on the neck, head, chest, abdomen, liver, or other body parts. I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple wounds on the head because my memory will come into play in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or the head is involved, and if no bones are broken, take care to determine whether it's caused by stone or similar things, and if the skin has been fully torn and the wound is large, you lightly doubt abscess formation: in such case, perform immediate surgery on the cephalic area immediately if there is little blood from the wound, and treat accordingly depending on which part was affected; and allow the patient to drink a fullness of wine and consume heavy meats afterwards.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they don't want to undergo surgery, if they reduce their meat intake, and do not drink wine, nor eat heavy meats; and place on the wound, if an abscess forms there, moist cotton in rose oil or in a wine that stops bleeding. And if there's no significant abscess formation, place it on the fresh wound, as long as it retains all its blood, and isn't disturbed by air. Use the powder I will mention shortly; and if it has been disturbed by air, apply some ointments until they heal completely.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a tailor and similar, and the lips cannot be joined together by stitches, then join them with suturing, as I would say for wounds in the belly, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes the bone, and if it stops for a bit only in one place, then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin. Command the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles, cooked wheat, like peas, and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover a putrefaction, and it does not reach the bone, then remove the putrefaction entirely, and bleed out; then treat it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without clotting, and cannot be stopped with medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find that it has been dislocated, fix it with a thread; and if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder which binds like this when the heat has affected it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way to use the powder is as follows: take part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; living charcoal three parts, and finely ground powdered, then apply it to the wound, and press it firmly until it aerates well and joins with all its blood; then tie it tightly, and leave it untouched if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And this must be done with a salve alone, not with incense or the blood of dragons, but when the medicine has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has healed the wound, immediately in that state, neither oil nor this powder should be applied; but ointments prepared beforehand or oat flour mixed with water and honey are to be placed there until it drains. Then other treatments can continue until the patient is well.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone fracture accompanies the wound and it's small, then use fine needles to fix it; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	from the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound originates near the neck and is straightforward, if there's no distinction between it and beneath the chin, but if something within the neck or artery has been cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, let no treatment follow except for its natural cure, and don't apply anything restrictive; doing so harms the nerves and causes them to recede. Don't put anything cold on the wound as nerve substance is inherently cold, and its continuity is with the head which is the highest part of the body; instead use warm medicine such as water lilies in gentle water, mixed with rose oil, and similarly washed cucumbers in gentle water, along with other ground substances in this manner. Apply moist ointments too.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it tightly with bandages, then treat until it heals properly.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with blood, you must puncture or go deeper; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, you should open it up, sew it, and cauterize as required; and if the windpipe has been cut, or the ribs, and the passageway is preserved, through which meat travels, so that the rib rests on the throat bone, but not touch the throat, let it be done according to its natural shape; and then make a fit addition, and leave for several days, then treat with desiccated ointments until healed; and if there appears an impression in the bone, you should remove; and if there are pieces of bone, if they can all be removed, take them out, but leave any that cannot reach; let the wound heal, and drain thoroughly from its source; and if the wound is fresh, apply a powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has an abscess, treat it as described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	From the wound of a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, look to see if there's an outward breeze near the wound site: you'll know that the wound is mortal; and if it isn't deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't apply powder at the first hour nor bind it up for fear of bleeding too much and replenishing in the depth of the wound, leading to heart strain. But instead use an attractive ointment and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton into the wound to suck out moisture and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so long as there's no spasm nor tremor of heart, and once you see good signs you'll know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat with various remedies and other treatments until it heals; and if it cannot heal and work, know immediately that there is a fistula; conduct the treatment as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple or worse or on the back, depending on how to treat the one in front; if it's large, stitch treatment; and if it's small, powder treatment; and if it's seeping into bone, and has extracted pieces, then you know about the wound, and remove the impurities; and if they are not removed, leave the wound to heal on its own, if aids in extracting (impurities); and for other wounds on other limbs, judgments are similar as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	From the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Abdominal injuries are large, medium, and small; from a major wound it may have any of the intestines or parts of the intestines, by means of insertion of foreign bodies; and stitching is more troublesome and in no case is worse than smaller wounds compared to larger ones, because we can insert the intestines back repeatedly if they are not already returned piece by piece; because when the intestines swell from the cold, they do not return properly into position. And you should know that a rupture of the abdomen occurs through four ways: the two common stitches occur during abdominal closure, and other stitches for other body parts also have common closures with other wounds; however, they are even more suitable with the closure of the abdomen, and I will mention each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I state that when the wound is small, and no part of the intestine is involved, and if there's any damage it can be healed by one of two methods: either because of the size of the wound as we have mentioned, or due to the fact that the intestines are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him in this way: soak an sponge or dip a cloth in warm water only, or cook him in hot water with vinegar and pepper and garlic, until the intestines are released from swelling; and after each time you perform this treatment, make sure to release his breath so he can deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you notice the swelling dissipating, rinse or heat the intestines with water or wine and make sure they are cooked until tender, because with this method, digestion can handle only a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then widen a bit of the wound using the instrument by which one removes hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be to relieve any pain, not to cut without substantial need; and these are the tools for incision: you cut inside in the curve and outward not, and visualize this pattern:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines escape, if you can set them back according to their natural shape in their own proper place, because this is what matters, for it counts.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is broad, and it's in the belly area, you should make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head. And if the injury is in the belly region, place their head and bottom higher than the parts below; similarly, when the abdominal rupture is in one of the two sections, adjust so that the part being repaired is higher than the other; and thus you should follow what I'm explaining about large and smaller wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use whatever is at hand. Use the sacred needle which pierces through all the tears with its tip across the entire wound, and join the edges; this is a common way of stitching, and you should thread one or more needles depending on the size of the wound's width. Leave an inch from the edge of the wound as space, and insert your needle at that spot, leaving plenty of strong thread; then pierce both sides through the skin with both ends of the suturing instrument which is inside the skin, until you have pierced through that part completely, and join the three points together; then sew using a double strand of thread on either side of the needle. Then join the edges of the wound properly, leaving an inch as space, then insert another needle; then sew with this thread like your first stitch, stopping only when all of the wound is held in place; use needles that are medium-sized, between slender and thick ones because slender needles cut through all flesh, and very thick ones can't fully enter: so they should be medium sized. Don't stick them too deep into the flesh and skin for fear of cutting and worsening the wound when stitching; then tie up their ends to prevent bleeding during sleep, and cover their points with cloths or bandages until the wound is healed; this way of sewing works best in small wounds because you use only one needle for a second stitch which is common, and it involves joining both skin sides and both suture points together on one needle with medium strength thread. When you have pierced all four points together, pull the needle back to where you started, as when stitching linen. Leave an inch space between each stitch as wide as two fingers; this stitch heals the body, and I stitched a wound that was once made by a knife across the belly, which was torn with scissors, and the wound was more than one palm wide, it contained several intestines of two palms in length, and lay in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine until it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in an area where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put new clean cloth twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and start from the outer side until it enters within; when it has pierced through the flesh straight in and out, then guide the head towards the siphon or stitch line where you have entered the needle, and make another puncture on the inner side until it pierces the outer part; and with this stitching method, you do so as the leathersmith sews fur, leaving a gap of the siphon from one side, then take hold again from the other, until the entire suturing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen described correctly, is as follows: none of them perform this naturally by uniting the two parts together and placing one needle close to the other, doing it in this manner: use a needle or point similar to that of the silk thread, make only one incision on this side, then leave both ends of the silk thread. Then turn the needle and make an incision from below through to inside by both ends of the silk thread; next make two more incisions on both sides coming down to the inside by using two other needles or points that are from the opposite end. This is the manner of suturing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word and none testify against it - that one should stitch the belly with two needles, each having thread in them. And you must sew one needle from one side, and the other from the other, as those who stitch corroies do; know that when the wound is midst the belly, the stitching there is more grievous than of their others for the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgements of the wound are similar to those of other wounds: and this is that when you find the fresh wound filled with all its blood, just as the surgeon has treated it, then sew up the intestine, and the skin; afterwards place on a stimulating powder over it, and if the surgeon has treated it, then apply no ointment at all until the wound heals; and change the stitches, and have them joined by the suture, and the dressing; then treat the wound as usual until it is healed; and if you lack medicines, then for now when it begins to heal properly, use old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine besides those in several preparations for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound may affect the principal limbs, it is necessary to soak light wool in oil heated with heat or in rose oil, and put it inside the joints, and apply it around the elbows; and if pain or gangrene occurs at times, then perform a bowel cleanse with black wine, and similarly if gangrene appears up to the intestines; and puncture inside, and know that when it's the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called 'the young' cannot heal when it's injured, and this is due to the position of the veins involved, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approach of its nature towards nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the bone jumps out of the wound, if you reset it back in the same manner as the intestine, while it is still fresh; and if it has aged and turned brown or black, then it is necessary to tie up what is black there, so that no blood comes through, because there are veins and arteries; then cut into the skin where the wound is, and place both ends of the bone below the wound until outwards for easing extraction when the bone jumps back in, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it can be restored in some animals, as I have seen that a healthy person was pierced by a lance or through their stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach and became stenotic, causing loss of appetite and gas. I applied treatment according to my knowledge, not stopping until it healed completely, and sutured the intestines.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it fused together, I wondered if the patient might have hurt himself in his belly. There was no harm, but he stayed in much better conditions, eating and drinking; and an experimenter said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated like this: take large leaves, then join the edges of the wound together, and once the leaves have opened their mouths, place them on the two edges so that they force her mouth up. And then close the leaves, and hold them in such a way that they cannot escape, then put another leaf after this manner, as before, until all the wound is covered; and thus the wound heals.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	In the case of inflammation in the intestine and no harm to the patient, there is no difficulty in joining the intestine using a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine, as follows: take the beginning part of this intestinal thread that is most hollowed out, then tie it with a fine thin linen thread, afterwards knot the thread on the needle and sew through the intestine. And stitch it at the opening; and this way of sewing threads is only according to the route of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the bowels, there being no organ or muscle involved, because of the fineness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, as it matures, is universally termed 'fistula', and even when hairy and round in shape.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the true swelling of hardened and white tissue, where no pain is felt, and it is also covered like a bird's feather; and at times it appears clear in shape, and at other times thickened; sometimes small, and at other times quite large; and I have spoken about this under the division of wounds: that every wound which has not healed and contains no flesh, leaving only through one of the eight causes: this means by a tiny flow of blood or pus; or due to its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the skin, which doesn't allow new tissue to form; or there's too much pus; or your veins or bones are diseased, and the matter is of poor quality; or because the medicine used isn't good for treatment; or it behaves like a pestilence due to corruption; or because digestion and health are delayed in that region, and then overcome by nature; or if there are veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, along with their signs, and treatments with medicines under the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	So it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that originate with large veins and arteries, and nerves, either inside or outside the thorax, or intestines, or bladder, or any part on the ribs, or spinal column, or joints of hands or feet; and indeed if they come to affect the primary property of the main limb, or their characteristics.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this manner are in need of healing, and there is no other cause but injury or ignorance; and if any fistula does not lead entirely to its root as I have said, then you are at the point of treating it, and you come to recognize it. Take a spider web tent or iron, should the fistula be straight, take it; and should the fistula be twisted, seek out a subtle plumb line tent, for the plumb bobs will bend with movement along its twist. Should this fistula have lost tips that cannot properly be sought after by tents, flush it with a catheter through one of these lost tips, as moisture is conducted from one to another through them; then cleanse it carefully with your strength, knowing if there is bone or nerve within, and it goes all around in fullness. Ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press their hand, and where that point lies. And once you truly know that point and whether it's far from a joint, or bone, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I've mentioned, if your method follows what I have said, remove the pus and decayed matter within; then treat it until it has healed properly. If this fistula is well and truly deep in its right place, it's fitting to fill it fully with a forceful technique, as much as you can manage, then insert wet bandages soaked in medicinal water in from that point at the top of the fistula, allowing the medicine to corrode what remains left within. Then apply healing salves until it has truly healed; and if it hasn't healed through this, cauterize it just as we've said, and should bone be corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If you do not obstruct the vein or principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there's decay and darkness, one must drain it until all decay has been removed. Then cleanse it with healing ointments until it heals properly; and if it does not heal properly and returns to its original condition as before, you should know that this far you are on your journey: keep uncovering and treating until you reach the bottom, remove all the decay, then restore it in place; and if it remains healed like this, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If it is not like that, you should know that the corruption has become too extensive, you cannot restore it; if there's nothing but to let it follow its natural course. And if there's a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with forceps, use an appropriate instrument for this task. If there are many bones affected, remove them all, do not leave even one. And if moisture causes contradiction, with no fear or caution, operate, handle the moisture, and cleanse the bones, freeing them from their attachments.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something against the wound that aids in putrefaction and leave it until the flesh is thoroughly rotten inside the bone, then they will break more easily; and if it's a large bone like from the leg or thigh, only continue with the corruption process until all of the blackness has been removed, then heal the wound; and if there's a great part of the putrefaction that extends to the bone, you should remove and cover up until right at the point of decay, then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in someone's leg where you can take an example and guidance for your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, until the substances reached the leg, and he developed a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the surgeons worked on it so aggressively that when they opened the abscesses, they ate away at a lot of flesh, and it became a fistula. And many people suffered a great deal from the body's pus and moisture; and for two years, many surgeons attempted treatment, with no expert knowledge in the art of surgery until I was called, and I examined his leg and treated him with medicines intended to heal him, along with what was eating away at the body through the defects; and the parts of the body became red from youthfulness, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these depressions, and then searched all the depressions, finding that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurriedly did then, and cut into one of the depressions until I uncovered a part of the bone, finding that it was rotten and perforated. I observed that the corruption extended all the way inside the bone; I identified this as the sign appearing from the rotten bone, assuming there wasn't any further corruption beyond what I saw; and began to heal the wound with medicines over an extended period, unable to stitch it up. Then I started again, uncovering the bone in the same manner, finding that the corruption continued within the bone. I treated it accordingly and removed it, worrying about stitching up the limb. However, I could not do so because I cut into a part of the bone roughly half its width, and it was healed over entirely by all its flesh; then I applied medicines to treat it; and it healed rapidly and did not require further work on the operation except due to the weakness from fear caused by illness, which couldn't be endured, and due to my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For blood evacuation often occurs, but it was completely healed. In its place of the bone, a hard flesh formed, and it had good disposition and didn't cause any harm or opposite effect at all from beginning to end, neither inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, as it should be treated in this manner: take a thread and pull at the end of the bone that is open, and command it to extend upwards; and put another thread of thicker fabric than the first thread, and tie it over the flesh that is inside the bone, pulling on its head so that you remove the rotten flesh below, exposing the flesh where the bone should be, making sure not to harm the flesh; place a poker or a table under the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and continue treating until as much corruption can be seen and felt, and treat again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is decayed and does not open, and corruption exists in middle or a part of it, then reveal all the flesh. Then put the brand over it and then pass the corruption with your hand from one side to another. And allow the healing process as long as the corruption lasts; just as we said before; and if corruption is within the joint, correct the corrupted joint, and open or cut through the bone on the other side; and if corruption is in continuation of two joints, there should be no other angle than that of the connection; and if corruption is at either end of a finger or toe, it may seem very difficult but you must still seek to identify this corrosion as to how it opens; then cleanse every part using all possible methods without opposing the skin or nerve. Know that the cutting tool and needles for treating bones vary depending on the arrangement of bone pieces, the appearance of the wound, its size and subtlety, its dimensions large or small, toughness; accordingly, you need to choose an appropriate instrument according to each type of operation. Know that your experience will reveal what tool is needed based on knowledge of this craft and observation of disease patterns; then think about the appropriate tool as per necessity, considering it wisely.
dou feu	by fire
