Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein so are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then change the blood, and it begins the vein to exit outwards, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder is open, it should be wrapped around with a piece of wood of one and a half to two thirds, and bind it, and let the wood remain on the leg. And every time there's need for more, wrap it in again along with the wood, and if it's too long, cut off a part, wrap it back on, but don't cover its root until all is out. Because if you cover it, it enters the flesh and causes pus formation and decay or disease; so it should be treated little by little up to half length, without leaving anything behind. And there mustn't be any time when this vein has been treated for five palms long, or ten, then one hand's worth from me, where the wood comes out of ten palms long, and when you cover it, keep a ring or piece of the tendon, and drill until all is out; and empty the contents that are inside, and apply healing remedies without any pus for a day, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein with cold hands, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or ankle, causing much damage, and where there is a break; then treat it accordingly as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "the cow disease", because it has often affected cows, and it's a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body upwards and downwards. The pain is felt at the onset from one limb to another, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and then it jumps; and it is infested with pus from some fluids, such as worms, snakes, roundworms or threadworms in the stomach; one wonders about its maliciousness because when it travels through the body, and when it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters and destroys the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot do much when it happens: hence, it is necessary that you bind the arm above and below with a strong rope very tightly, then cut upwards and force out the pus, and if it moves into the flesh, and you don't find it, then cauterize it with fire until it heals; and any major damages it causes, are when it hits the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, then bind around him the eye form, then cut upwards, and force out; and it is necessary to use the hand of purification from body medicines of soluble substances for illnesses caused by bad humors, and be wary of meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into any limbs, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to attend a sick woman and saw her arms uncovered. I noticed a small swelling in the vein of her arm. Soon after, I observed it ascend as if a worm moving up to her shoulder, faster than anything else, just like molten silver when it's cut away from its source; the pain left that part of her body and entered her shoulder. Then later, it spread throughout her entire body until it reached the other arm; then she began complaining about pains within her body as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how it moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never seen this disease in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to ensure that the movement of pain from one part of her body to another had been done properly, but I did not do it myself as I observed in this woman; and I thought that was due to her having a dry body, with exposed veins, and because of this constraint wind becomes visible; and does not become apparent according to this reason for those who are luxurious and have moist bodies and their veins closed up.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it has opened as we said, then press upon and around it quickly, and then apply pressure until that constriction of air escapes out; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see this at your fingers, treat him who debouted the air, such as foul pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	The phrase "des saiettes" refers to arrows or projectiles that may be embedded in wounds. It is often used in medical texts of the medieval period when describing treatments for injuries caused by projectiles, such as those sustained from battles or hunting accidents.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety in their nature is that some have large points, and small ones, and those that are barbed or fused together. Others have two angles, and there are those with tongues, and those where pieces exist; and among these arrows, some that don't release anywhere do so according to different ways: Some discharge primarily in major limbs, such as the head, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and other major body parts.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the chest thus is in no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, presents itself: it becomes necessary for you to undertake the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in several dispositions; and when that bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not been entirely extracted, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow penetrates and pierces the bone, is when there is bleeding from a wound above the brain, it's also when blanching, swelling, and inversion occur in the eyes, as well as redness of the tongue, and convulsions along with confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes it affects neither nose nor ears; and sometimes it results in loss of speech and voice; and bleeding from the wound appears white like pus, and also burns like flesh; and if that sign appears, you should attend to treatment, remove the arrow if it hasn't.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the needle when it bites or pierces is that it's near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck into something hard, not empty; and accidentally the needle also ceases like a pulse, with black blood coming out, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never lets out pus is when there's no foam bursting from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with a cold chill.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the buttocks cover, it's deep in the back; and there is great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders are moving.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, by chance if there's any undigested flesh from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach is hit, and there's no meat passing through the intestines in the jump, then there's no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder, and urine flows out during the jump, and patients feel intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, forearm, back, thigh, leg, and similar limbs, are safe depending on various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is within your nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because that's how you should handle such a situation.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one of the servants that an arrow fell into his left rib near the nose: I probed it and pulled it out from the other side through the fat behind the ear, causing no serious harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow from one's play that had fallen into the fat behind the ear near the paper, and the arrow was stuck in such a way that only its tip pointed towards the shaft, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, with no metal to pierce the ears; the game went well, and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And remove an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the Arabic arrow was in his ear: I would cut off his whiskers, and skillfully extracted it as I pulled it out, and the Christian became well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And removed an arrow in my home, that was stuck in his chest or stomach, and I thought he would die; and then after passing thirty days, he didn't change his position. I cut on the arrow, pulled it out with forceps, and removed it, without any bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see in my home that an arrow has fallen or hit the back, and the wound was sealed up; and kept the arrow inside it, without changing its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And consider another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face, and the wound was stitched up; he then endured great pain for some time; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And one day an arrow was shot at the home of the princes' king, who had it stuck in his neck, and he was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was completely inside him. I was summoned for treatment three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be greatly constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried every method with great care and did not feel it; and he felt pain and discomfort around his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a drawing plaster and digestive one on him because his ears were not inflamed; and I noticed the ear of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice to her hands for several days, and treated the wound immediately, then had her rest for a long time afterwards. The patient felt a pain deep inside their nose each day over that period; and I explained this to them.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive mercury medicine to the wound for several days until it opened, then tried various treatments and felt the tip of the arrow moving towards its entry point. I filled the wound opening with that corrosive mercury until the head of the arrow became visibly evident; and kept treating it well for about four months, and then cleaned up so thoroughly that I was able to pinch off the entire wound edge from both sides, unable to remove anything further; therefore, I continued inventing various tools and methods to create instruments, just until one day I succeeded in using nicely crafted pincers according to what will be described at the end of this chapter. This way, I treated it and then left the wound to heal.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And those who judge decide that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it thusly, and after sealing the wound, and completely healed the patient.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I've told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so place your treatment on what I don't mention, because books can't understand everything; but wise doctors compare well on quite a few small things, and based on what is present and lacking, they find new works, and new tools, for the removal of foreign objects that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows penetrate the limbs where they are stuck according to two methods: either through the side where they enter or from another direction; and the one that enters or goes in this way, it is an arrow penetrating the flesh, and such arrows now no longer occur.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it be until the body heals internally, and the discharge comes out; similarly, if it's stuck in bone and can't come out, leave it like that for a few days, and try to remove it every day; then it will jump. If it doesn't, pierce internally with all subtlety until the chest is enlarged, as long as the ribs internally are spread wide, then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the head, and goes up to one of the stomachs at the brain, or any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear before the patient: do not remove it immediately, but leave it until she is equal after a few days, because if the arrow reaches this far, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and not to its full depth, and does not pierce any organ, causing no harm for days without a bad event, then the removal device for extraction should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly stuck like this and can't come out by force, then administer internal remedies, as I've told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow has penetrated within the body so deeply that it cannot be seen, and you have to rely on feeling alone for its location; and if you sense it, try extracting it without any suitable instrument; and if you can't due to the size of the wound or depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins involved, then extract as much as necessary leaving a large wound. Once you feel it, pull out the arrow if possible, and if it has ears that hold it in place, remove the flesh stuck on both sides until you can cut it off; then break or bend the ears of the arrow, continuing as long as needed to extract it; be sure not to break the arrow, as this would make its extraction harder.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't achieve it in one go, until the arrow reaches your hand, let it get stuck there, then pull it out because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if bleeding during the procedure contradicts you, then follow what we have advised about treatment in our chapter; and be cautious with incisions near nerves and veins, and use technique to safely extract the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to their position when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that it should be like that. If you cannot do so, then place them according to what the symptoms show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that came from the other side, or where no part of it is visible or feels swollen when you see or touch it: then cut upwards as far as your forceps can grasp, and then pull: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, turn your hand around, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then guide it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it can't come out, leave it and start extracting again until it does; and if there's still part of the arrow inside when you see or feel it, press firmly over the entire length of the shaft; and if it is at the tip, if you apply pressure evenly, then use your tool with a curved tip so that the arrow point goes into the curve of the tool; and then push hard, and if the arrow is caught in place, then press the tool where its tip enters to facilitate extraction.

des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body

des sainies de ventouse	of suction healings

And do not sleep afterwards, it is necessary for them to warm up, when they should be sucked and when they have been sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch for those who are purging and are of hot temperament, and if they are too vigorous and inflamed; it is necessary for them to consume cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and moist lettuce, and similar items; and they should eat small portions, and meat from castrated animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with cold constitution should consume honey syrup and moderately fragrant old wine. They should eat small portions and small pieces of meat from castrated animals as well as little birds and young pigeons. On the day they are to be treated with suction cups, they should drink more than they eat; it is necessary for some individuals to give them senna or muscat before or after treatment in order to strengthen their main limbs. Keep the belly cool but avoid having those who are hot consuming it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups meant to cause injury are those placed on the liver, and under the kidneys, and in gout, and on the belly and groin. This member does not suffer from being injured by punctures, and it is done forcefully only to draw blood from one part of the body to another; similarly we place them on nipples when newborns are healthy; for removing viscosity present in parts, we also apply suction cups under the belly and on the groin for reducing the size of that part. It relieves pain when there's swelling or stone, it can remove a lump by its attractive power accidentally, or vacuums out the stone from its place; thus it operates when placed under the liver and kidneys where viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are used empty to suck only once; they are not used together with fire in any case, and some are filled with boiling water or with water that has cooked herbs suitable for this purpose, so one might fill a suction cup with hot water from this source.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers wide and half a palm in length, and at its middle one small notch is made, as to pierce like an awl, either of an animal or iron, such that when placed on the body it does not hurt the patient; and there is a metal rod in the middle, be it from an animal's leg bone or iron, for placing a candlewick, with them being large and small depending on the illnesses and age of those using them; because children's suckers are different than adults', and those from thin people are different than those from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And we should thus place this sucker on the body: hold the candle or thread in place, and insert it through the rod inside the sucker so that the light is at the bottom of the sucker, preventing it from burning the patient; then place it on the body, with your fingers on the notch as we have described, so that when desired, if vapor starts coming out, remove the sucker; and hold the thread in the same way, repeating often, should you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in pleurisy disease, at all acute times, there's neither a needle nor a point used, and it's only administered forcefully when it's full of water, and placed solely on the limb; and that's its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Poultices are administered only in limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in those shaved bald, like ears or armpits, and other similar conditions. The quality of the poultice is that when you find poultices that are in gentle water without impurities, you take them; then immerse them in gentle water until they become familiar and have nothing in their stomachs; and then cleanse with a vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the poultices on it. And when they're full and secrete, if there's a part where a suction cup can be placed, you do so, as this is of great value afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the arm with hot water first, and then cold water quite well, and afterwards apply oil. And if it's still inflamed too long after the cuts of veins, moisten a linen cloth in cool water and place it on, until the cut heals; and if there are multiple cuts, apply powdered vitriol or garlic, and similar actions, until they heal; otherwise put half-cooked peeled beans under the arm, and leave them so that they dry out on the arm, which will stop the bleeding immediately. And if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take well to healing, rub with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until blood comes out and then place on it; once they smell the blood, they will start to heal immediately. And when you see that they are discharging pus, powder them lightly with some aloes and powdered meal, or ashes, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fracture and alleviation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear child, that the people of this chapter gaze upon what's contained within it, something unseen in ancient books or letters read; hence this knowledge has been extricated from our land, as I've never found any good content before. And I know nothing, for it comes from the study of ancient books, to which I have devoted much effort and time, through experimentation, and through habit with my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained within, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly illustrated the forms of instruments used, as done in the two chapters preceding these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we outline or introduce this book's main points and chapters where the wise people use their understanding, and remain faithful to truth. Let those who have experienced this know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or stiffness occur to any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if there's nothing pressing on them, such as weakness, children, old people; or if their pulse isn't steady, too fast, too weak; and cold fluids, meaning cold jades, and eye and parsley flesh, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats. And don't let your meals be too heavy with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of pus coming from an abscess or spreading of matter in the limb; if the patient begins to improve under their first management, as they were using it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that cause a heavy digestion or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and nuts, and pies, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, after an operation, it can move again more quickly than the breaking.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that old and weak bones cannot be restored or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of limbs, nor are those too soft, such as the bones of young children; but do this, set again the broken bone with a big mallet on the protruding pieces that separate and join the limb together, until it supports like before. And don't finish his work straight away, for this is suitable, feed him with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from the fracture of the heel, or of the leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others through cutting, such as the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with injury, or a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner it has its own tool and its proper instrument in the restoration process, according to what memory brings to mind; and is known by the breaking of the bone when the limb is twisted, opening well outward, and feels pressing from the hand; and when there is no twisting or rubbing, and the patient doesn't feel much pain, if there is no breakage; but it can have twisting, or cracking, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But do not move it with your hand yourself, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage which was in action, and were the two parts separated, they should now put them equal, so as to make incisions close together; and if incisions are too close, let him not leave it for any day, until the incisions heal; then place him evenly under your skillful and gentle touch, knowing that its restoration is easier than the restoration of those with pieces; then tighten, according to what should be done after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, and it's divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or by your hand is a small member, or at two strings, or one string and by your hand; place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb have been removed, you pull them in every way with force onto their places as much as you can, and be careful not to cause the patient any injury or pain; and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And hold it well in your hand if you feel that it is not properly set: if it is dressed beautifully, and do not over-tighten, do not press as they do when they remove an abscess by their method of incision and contraction on the limb, as we have desired many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, make sure to control the patient so they do not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, neither upon turning or in any other way; ensure that the limbs are firmly secured so no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when they do not feel any pain, it is not properly in place and you should arrange them so that they do not feel any pain. And guard that they are put correctly, so that there is no crookedness upon their restoration; and the quality of the broken limb must be according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied by size and extent and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And for small limbs like arms and legs and alike: they must be enveloped in soft and fine linen; and those that are larger, such as thighs and calves: they should be enveloped in wide, sturdy bandages since the wide bandages encompass the entire large limb equally from all sides, without causing any unevenness. Then loop thin linens lightly around three or four times according to the limb's size, and press your hand on every part of the bandage slightly. Afterwards proceed above the break and apply less pressure so that it doesn't move away a bit from the break; and soften the bandage little by little until you have treated almost all of the healthy part, then take another linen loop, wrap it around the broken limb again, and return to the vicinity of the break, applying moderate pressure without going too hard or too soft. This is as we explained in the first part above. Then place linens or bandages between the loops until they are evenly distributed throughout; afterwards cover them all with a bandage, and then fit your well-made pins onto it, unless there's pus or inflammation present.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is inflammation or an abscess, then apply something soothing for the abscess and that reduces the swelling. Let it stay like this for a few days; then stretch your limbs, and they should be at half the width of a small cane reedly cut straight, or from the shafts used to make clamps, or palm fronds, and do so according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the limbs which one places on the brace be slightly larger and wider than the others; and they should also be as long as suitable to the size or grandeur of the limb. Then stretch them onto the braces in the same manner you did at the first attempt, then attach a compensation thread above, just like you did on the fracture initially; make it tighter now, but not excessively; and it is necessary that the threads are moderate, neither too large nor too small, and they should be made of soft linen. For if the thread is too thick, as in works made by those who perform their bindings with twisted linen cords, this is a great mistake because the binding cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it is not suitable for there to be less than half a finger's width between each limb.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the edges of the stitches after tightening during their healing, then place linen patches or raveled wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the ribs are broken, I will then describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to hold back too much of your efforts when healing broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, one should not use these plasters immediately after three or four days or even more depending on the abscess that appears; and here is the way of using ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: you take flour that stands in mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is a common method for restoring fractures in multiple orientations, as well as for pregnant women and young children since there are no restrictions on its use whether hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take three parts of each of these: barley meal, dandelion, rue, and asafetida, along with gum arabic and myrrh; measure it out to be .x. three times the amount specified for each individual ingredient. Mix in a bit of myrrh and aloes also at .v. five times. Add seven parts of alechil (a type of vinegar). Grind all ingredients into powder, then mix with plenty of egg. If the mixture is warm to touch, use this plaster; it has good composition properties and rapidly heals broken bones and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering for torsions: take mugwort and wormwood, each measure IX thirds; myrrh and aloes, each measure IXI thirds; carageena, measure VI thirds; Armenian boric acid, measure X thirds, grind them well, mix with water or plenty of egg whites, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones where they are, and relieve the pain that follows, and use bone cutting tools and hot oil for bruising: take new wool, and fat in a pot cooked with oil, and apply it on your limbs.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Bandages do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses, and properly treating the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial plantain leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster is for the restoration of bone fracture and to relieve the removal of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of parsley, chamomile, violet flowers, fennel flour; from each take one part; grind and mix with wine, then if your limbs are warm, mix it with wet coriander water, or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more forcibly than the first, when pus is returning to the recovery of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and linseed, balsa wood, marjoram, and sage, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all take one part; and grind it, and mix with salt water or sweetened water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that only beeswax ointment made of wax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration without anything else. He states that it must not be too soft or too hard but just right.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, substances slightly heated and somewhat dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to prepare plaster for injury and pain: take mung beans and chicken feathers from cooked chickens, or bird feathers, and basil leaves, and sand equally ground, grind them, make the mixture into plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then after a little time, take care not to let the patient feel any pain or move their bone from its place. If you don't remove the plaster in hand motions, and if pain starts in the limb, or itching, without rest or swelling, then act quickly, remove the plaster, and apply fresh bandage immediately; use a light cloth and wet sponge, soak them in water, and cool down the limb until the itching stops and the pain is relieved. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put it on dry wool, moistened with water or oil, and bind it with a strip of linen until you are sure of pus presence; cool down the inflammation in the limb, relieve pain, then continue with careful reapplication, and a little plaster, do not apply too firmly as before; be careful until the patient is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus is coming out and the area is red, painful, swollen and oozing, indicating inflammation throughout, then you will need to apply plaster and bind it, start again as you did initially, in exactly the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there is no effect on the limb as we have said, or it isn't released until after three days or four or five or seven; and let him not rest any time then, according to what can be seen, until inflammation subsides, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh above; therefore maintain your restraint more than before, and allow his body to swell its substance as I have said previously; and if you see that the skin has dried excessively beyond what is necessary, know that bruises will not come about; thus dip him in hot water every time you release him, and do this once every three days, and clean a little around the wound; with this work then cut off the bruise on the limb, quicken this operation compared to what foolish practitioners do, who forcibly straighten the limb: this is bad practice, and it is wasteful effort, and I see nothing else than allowing and operating him directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding various methods of breaking bones
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and various forms are there, with causes being distinct; for some fractures are made by the impact of a sword, and necks fracture all the bone up to the symphysis which is near the bone, such as done by a hammer or staff; hence this manner of breaking is called "hatchet break".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this is called "absolute" fracture; and these are either large or small wounds resulting from such fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or fracture of the stone collarbone, or under the stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture partly through, which approaches until it reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that heals within the bone as thin as hair, and has small cracks, this kind of break is called "hairline"; and if the wound is made by hitting with stone or falling or any similar thing, and has the piece of bone inserted downward, and the pieces are close together just like blacksmiths when they forge on the anvils; if a piece goes inside the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more in those with softer bones, like children's heads; and occurs in all these manners of fractures where small fragments are lost like feathers; and I shall speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all methods of breaking through the diminution upon them, and the examination by touch, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs inside it, if the breakage shows black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware of any bad accidents due to illness, if you see no harmful incident, such as vomiting bile, loss of intellect, extension and rigidity, fever ague, and if the eyes emerge and turn red, or show other similar symptoms in various conditions, you cannot be certain of recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in winter, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day after the month; so that when the pus around the bone becomes infected, and accidents as we said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of the bone comes up to the fabric that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut into the fractured part like this: and take hold of the edge of the patient's unbroken head, and expose the bone in all ways possible, and more accurately based on the appearance of the wound. If blood starts to flow during exposure, or if pus forms, use what is appropriate then place a wet cloth soaked in rose oil inside the gap; let the wound rest until the pus subsides, and make sure there is no more bleeding. Then begin working into the bone according to two ways of operation: one way involves cutting at the narrowest part facing front, which defines its shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut that is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different size cuts, some narrow and others wide, all pointed and made of iron; and execute them lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, it's necessary for you to pierce through internally, so that you make cuts with needles, not fully piercing until beyond the bone surface, and there should be a margin or about half a circle above the point, ensuring the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each goes into its place of the bone's thickness, so that you have needles for all parts; and this is the form of the three types of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the needle in another spot a bit after, and do this for all around, then cut out the space of the bone which is between the teeth, doing it more finely than you can and gently as we said, as long as you bring the bone to your hand or any tool you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain nor the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have punctured and cut the bone, it is appropriate to clean off any remaining bone debris with an instrument resembling a scissor but which should be more robust and finer than another scissor; if there's nothing left of small bones or scales, gently scrape them away using those instruments. Then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing this is as Galien taught, which is more safe; and it uses strong tools, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, it is necessary to uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture opens and moves, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, from which its shape is given:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and make the cut across in two sides, so that when cutting you are against the bone; then with a small hammer at hand, so you can lightly stroke over the whole bone, and be well careful of the cloth which is underneath; if it sticks to the bone, then gently scrape it off the bone, for this scraping does no harm and causes no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture doesn't penetrate just to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, with small pieces present, then after that abrasiveness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor you must have in various quantities, for administering the most suitable one to each area according to the treatise and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are in front of large razors, and after even finer ones, and never cease doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other scalp cuttings and finer fractures, it is necessary that you apply treatment according to their orientation; and this matter is not answered by someone who has put their study into this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the scab is uncovered, it is necessary that you use linen of the size required for the wound, soak it in oil rose, and place it over the wound; then take another layer of doubled linen, soaked in wine and oil rose, and place it above the first layer. Do this more lightly than you can, making sure not to weigh down the scab, then administer bandage again from above with a third layer, but do not pull tightly that it only touches the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess is somewhat calmed, then remove the bandage and apply medicine such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and aristolochia among others; make a powder from these things, put it over the wound, and then administer more gentle medicines without causing irritation. And beware that the wound remains clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor let it get stuck with dirt, for when dirt assembles under the cloth of the brain, it moves and irritates, causing great harm to the patient; because when something mordant is put over the scab, it becomes irritated from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then be careful therefore, if no accidents come to the patient as we have said, there is doubt without fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fear does not come out only due to the medicine that we have placed on it, should this substance possess such a virtue, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rooster's gall and an inch of glue, and spread this mixture on your skin. Then treat with methods appropriate for treatment until it is healed, while it remains healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that never are broken the two parts below the nose or only one of them, because they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous, it does not break, even if you bend or twist it, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should pinch or squeeze your small finger or nose tip, and apply the breakage evenly inside your index finger, and outward through your nostril. Continue this until your nose recovers its natural shape; do this gently, and be careful not to cause pain for the patient with your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and cannot come to the nostrils, it must be that you put it level with the tip of a hair a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the breakage is two parts, redo this procedure, and try to restore it on the first day if possible; if not, after seven or eight days when the abscess is calm, then pinch at the nose tip using linen cloth. If the breakage occurs in one part, do so accordingly.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another one from the other side, if the break is in that direction; and make them large enough to fill the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer thinks to moisten the warts with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.
