I don't think it's quite right, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a concoction from an egg, and powder of mill grind; then leave the wart until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes, one should use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have an egg, wrap it in them, and keep the warmth, allowing the air to circulate among the wounds; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you work on it, then apply a wet cloth or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little pot of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses are not developing, apply a poultice externally, made of ground snail shell and incense powder, mixed with an egg yolk. Then place it on light bandages, don't tie them tightly; and if they break without hurting the skin too much, and they break into small pieces, then use tools suitable for this purpose to extract, cut open the wound and cleanse it of all impurities, then suture it, using poultices and ointments suitable for this task. And if there is no wound beneath the skin, then treat the wart, and apply thyme needles until they heal.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured and there is no wound on the surface, and only the breakage is external, not at all broken into two halves but rather split internally throughout, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture occurs in the right part, to place your index finger in the mouth on the side of the injury; and if the fracture occurs in the left mandible, you should place your index finger of your right hand on the injured side, and gently apply pressure to the fracture internally, then press it outward with the other hand from outside, ensuring it is even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is divided into two parts, then it is necessary to provide extension for both halves, ensuring they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth start moving or break, or you have to stitch them back together using a thread of gold, silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken jaw and put two layers of linen on it. Place under one layer a large ridge made well or a piece of leather matching in length and width according to the jaw size. Secure this at the ends that you can reach and instruct the patient to rest, and let them consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then put things back in order according to what has changed; apply plaster, mixed with powdered materials or enough eggs or flour of chestnut, after removing the wax. Place a light woolen cloth over the plaster, and if the plaster dries and the patient's position remains unchanged, let them rest until they heal. Many times healing occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when pus comes out during an incision, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward nothing of the bone that has been removed; so much delicacy was required in using tools suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains nothing, if the wound is wide, place one plaster suitable for it over it to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	By the power of
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and the breaking occurs in three ways: sometimes it is broken and torn into two parts, resulting in fragments that are easier to restore; or there's tearing with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are as follows when there's tearing with an injury: you need two assistants, so that one marks the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other extends their arm towards the affected part. Then make the break equal with your hands, ensuring the shape matches what it should be, without any sign of strain or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder to the hair, and make its size according to your need; then stretch and lift up the force, hold the sponge in your hand so that you can make the break equal as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force outwards due to it coming forward, so that the patient lies on their back, and places a half pillow under their shoulder, and pushes the shoulder blade downwards, until the bone of the force is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply pressure with your fingers, and if you find fragments, it is necessary to cut through them; and gently pull the pieces apart. If the bone cannot join at any point from pressure, make a cut near one of your incisions; but place this tool on the force, in order to prevent leakage:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It appears like a spoon, and is not found within, and can be as wide as needed according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, as it is with the wound you made when treating the bones; and once sure there's an abscess in each, if you let that wound heal, and if the opening is small, or if you're unsure of any abscess, if you cover the wound with cloths and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes out, if moisture arrives, apply oil roses and vinegar and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The grinding of the bone when it is affected by wounds and size requires that you place on the bone the plaster mixture of mill powder and beaten egg white, then place light bandages on top. If necessary, put a wad under the heel. Then take a very large bandage about a palm wide, then place a double cloth bandage on top of the bandage, and cover it with plaster. Next, take a small stick three fingers wide and long, wrap it around this bandage so that only part of the bandage is hanging down, and place it above the injury. Turn the bandage upwards towards the neck, under clean and diseased areas; and adjust from each side. When you see that the healing takes hold at the wound site, and clearly sees that the stick does not move on top of the broken bone, then reward him every day, and when the stitches are removed, put it in his rest. And make sure that the pain subsides on its back, and place it during sleep under the heel to raise the shoulder up; if the swelling of the injury is relieved by aligning the shoulder, or you tie your arm around the neck, and do not remove it until bad things happen, for 20 days; then, if you see that there's need, renew the plastering and tighten and leave him like this, until he is restored. And she is restored in the longest of 28 days, but some people recover sooner.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A certain situation occurs when the shoulder is broken or fractured either at its end or mid-section; if it is dislocated only by external force. If you rearrange according to the shape of the break and reset it in line with its natural form, through any means possible. Then, apply a powder from the mill onto the joint mixed with plenty of egg whites, making light bindings, and place two layers over this. Next, lay out a large and fine strip somewhat larger than the shoulder across a wide piece of stone; ensure there is no movement anywhere on the shoulder; then cover that area with layers of linen wadding, making sure the strip fits evenly; afterwards bind it all tightly in one big band, so tightly that the stone doesn't move at its place. Keep an eye on your patient each day; and whenever they loosen up, readjust them, maintaining equal tension on the strip if it is not displaced from its place, laying the patient on their side; and by this method, the shoulder will be healed in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this period has elapsed, release the patient and ascertain that they are well, for what sets itself firmly cannot move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone piece appears first and not below the knee, then proceed by removing it, along with the abscess beneath, and do as we have instructed for treating wounds of muscle dislocation.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bones are broken once or twice in the middle, but this happens rarely; they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it tilts downward and the patient feels intense pain throughout their body, along with loss of consciousness, immediately afterwards, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the joints in the broken bones, and one can well perceive this.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it comes to setting the bone, should lie lay under his backbones, and you place one span between the shoulders, then press on the shoulders, and join the ribs of both sides with your hands, and gradually adjust them evenly in all possible ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plaster bandages over this fine structure of salt or another lightweight substance, wrap them in a piece of cloth, and tie them around the broken bone so that they do not move. Then bend the joint back onto the back, press against it properly, and reward every hour by massaging the wound area; if she begins to heal, then tighten her up; and if it is appropriate to remove, due to corrosion or itchiness coming from the body, or pain or abscess, act quickly, and loosen the tie, and remove the plaster bandage, and treat the person who came in with the cure methods. Then replace the bandage, and press it until it is fit for use.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs happens only in the large ones after the back and within, and do not bend because they are oily; and one feels it well during examination at the waist.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And for the healing process, you should make the break equal, just as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster and bind with a bandage if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is occurring internally, the patient feels great pain and piercing, like from labor pains, because the bone punctures the tissue; and they have pains all over, immediately and vomit much blood, and it's a serious health issue, and the elderly have experienced severe illness.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats which swell the belly, in order to expel the wind from outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this, for abscesses and pus do not come about unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it is said by none of us to apply suckling pigs over the wound in order to extract moisture and this appears reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup draws away excesses from the body due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that when treating the wound of an animal, one should cover it with moist wool in a hot oil, and place the bandages between the ribs to make the healing consistent all around. Then follow the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that cannot be borne by the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it's necessary to make an incision at the site of the broken rib, and you need to place a tool under the torn edge; and then one must cut through the bone, gently drain, and then suture the two edges of the wound if it's large, and treat with plaster until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have to drain pus, place it over moist cloths in oil and put them on the wound; then treat while that part of the body requires pus drainage, and have a constant watch on that side where it should be done, until it is cured.
de la brisure dou col	of the break at the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No fracture occurs at the bones of the neck, and it does not bend; similarly for the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to any person, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take care; if you see their hands softened, swollen, and dead, and unable to move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	You know that it is fatal in various conditions, and if they do not respond well when their limbs are restrained and there is no sensation, you know that the joint of the bone has been saved, and that the illness has been cured, as long as a treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when such a thing comes to the spinal column of the back, and you need to know if it is sane or not, take care that his joints are softened, and that any injuries are where they should be, and above the back ventosity and expulsion against will; and when it has been observed on its belly, it expels against will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is observed on his back and wants to sit up, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it's mortal: if you do not work diligently in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this incident does not happen to him, then it is a simpler thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should extract if there is pus, if it's placed on the spine or on the yolk of an egg, until it calms down; then place on one of the soothing plasters and let them dry, and bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they recover.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, then it should be covered with plaster; and remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if they're large, with stitches, then treat with ointment that heals flesh until it's healed; and if the tip of the bone is broken off, which is called 'the tip of the elbow', then you should hold your left hand pouch and place it evenly on the other to your power, then apply the plaster and bandage as needed; then press firmly, and if there are broken bones, then remove them and treat the wound until it's healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It occurs when the bone of the hip is broken. And if it happens, there should be a slight swelling at the knee; and it runs long, declines towards the groin, brings pain to the leg, and bruising, and inflates that which is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And in terms of restoration, you must extend your hand upwards, as long as you are over the breakage area; and understand where the breakage is and its shape. If the breakage is only at the knee, then make an equal breakage there, until it reaches a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is along the length of it or it declines towards the inside, then guide the patient so that they lie on their abdomen, as long as you are able to complete the repair of this breakage.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it evenly, set it on the plaster, then place it on a column of wood or charcoal, and hold the wound steady, so that it does not move; and apply the area over the ribs, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses swell up and come out, do not touch them until they are calmed down, and apply what we have already mentioned; then return to the process of treatment, tighten it as needed, assuming there is no bad incident; this is how you should proceed.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	From the breaking of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that lie between the handle and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of these two methods: wherein one method involves taking a full length staff of medium thickness, in this manner:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulder blades with two strips each, and place them on top, securing the patient's sides onto one spot. Then, lay the broken arm onto the staff until it reaches to the middle, making a bend of the staff halfway through, then rest it against any heavy object or let assistants hold it downwards; then place the broken end of the shoulder in alignment with his hands when they are together, up until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck, then instruct two assistants to have one cut off from where it's broken in his hands, and the other cuts off everything up to one finger length, stretching each one to its respective side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more fierce, then bind it tightly against the wound pain, and above the wound, and extend each of the assistants to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is close to the head of the shoulder, it should be necessary that you place one band in the middle against the seat, and the other towards the knife, against the wound; and also if the wound is towards the blade, then it should be necessary to place the band lightly, without effort, as long as the wound is equal on the left and on the blade; then make an incision evenly, just like it should, and hold tightly, so that no abscesses occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes out from it even after seven days, do not hold tightly any more; instead apply greased wool and oil roset, until the pus coming out is calmed down. Then hold tight, so when you place the plaster on the wound, then unite the arm with the shoulder support, put your hand on the shoulder or chest; apply the bandage and hold it tight both on the support and on the arm, ensuring that the arm stays straight, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you suspect that the bone does not move, use supports for this, and place a larger and stronger support under each cut than the others, leaving an inch of space between each support. Ensure that each support is large enough to pass through the wound three inches from both sides; then hold tightly on the supports as I instructed at the beginning of this chapter concerning wounds, more firmly but not stretching too far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the bed of the stumps, and the constriction, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken limb, and you hesitate about removing the clot, if you leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine each three days the tie, to ensure no itchiness spreads across the area or causes a rash, or that the infections cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such incidents occur, or if the dislocation takes longer than three days or more, and the patient feels better on his back and has his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cotton pad evenly filled with wool, and watch each hour of the day or from dawn, to see that the shape of the broken limb does not move or that the ties do not soften; if the address comes thanks to the power of medicine, and gives him back the meat we placed before him, in such a way that the meat becomes easily digestible at first; and when he begins to recover, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be readjusted every forty days from then; thereafter, one must relieve them, administer baths and medications for the wound to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightening is ugly and tangled, it should remain to be relieved for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the 'fosciles', from which one is small, and it's this that covers the pit; and the other is large, and it's this that rests under, near the small bone; by chance only the large foscile breaks or the small one, or by chance they both break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the healing; and when large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be slightly extended and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that's broken, you should pull more firmly; and extend him to the first cussin, and mark the hand pocket higher than the others, and place the small finger lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross his own ribs over himself, with the first cussin above him higher, so that the ribs don't suffer any labor; then extend your assistant's arm towards his side near his hand, or at the wrist, and another assistant above the other.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the eyes even, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, you place each one in its own location, and if there is none that grabs onto the bone, and you cannot restore it to its location, then do it upon and through the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is an injury due to the breakage, I spoke about it in the singular chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the commencement of the restoration, there come discharges that stick, then make a bandage of beeswax and white wax, so it should neither be too hard nor too soft; and bind this bandage properly from above in a fine manner, until the discharges that stick are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the wax, and put on the plaster of the powder from the mill with enough egg, then place the splints, and make sure that the splint for the fracture is more forward, and slightly wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints or arms in various positions: either that the break is within one bone, or in two; and fix it more on the fracture than anywhere else, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let those cloths above the fracture be soft and moistened, and do not make them hard or rough; and use threads made from linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the member and the link after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any harmful incidents occur to the member, such as itchiness that affects the member, it is necessary for you to dip the member in hot water, until the itching subsides; and let the member not be forced to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the process of ligature removal, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones have been exposed, and similar actions are taken.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no further constriction can come to the limb because it's too tight, it is necessary to soften it with heat and let it rest for a few days until the constriction ceases, then resume constriction.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, or if no untangling happens up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or elsewhere, then place their hands on their necks, and ensure that the necks are even, and take care not to move or disturb them, and let them rest on their back; know that this healing is restored in thirty days or forty-five, and sometimes in twenty, depending on the compositions and the temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that in the back of the hand and on us, few breaks occur, and only fold many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or folds, it should be treated by having the patient sit upright and directly in front of themself; then place their hand flat on the table and stretch out the fingers of the broken parts, and align the bones properly, making sure they are well connected; and apply bandages and splints, if no abscesses develop, then place an ointment according to the size of the injury; and wrap it in one linen sheet.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is at the base of the fingers near the belly of the hand sole, make a pyramid from cloths and instruct the patient to hold it against their broken finger; then stretch him with a long cloth, and place the splint as high as the size of the hand's palm, making sure it stretches properly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the front, it must be that you place one splint above and another below on the foot part. So that your hands are open and straight; then tie them entirely around the hand, and seal the joint between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the two feet, it's like a bundle, just as should be; and press with the heel, and if you see fit to place a small upright splint to raise the fracture, and not move. And if the break is at the other foot, like in the index or one of others, it's like a bundle, and tie with the healthy one which comes after; or you tie all together, as long as they can hold, or place an upright splint just like for dressing; and take care in restoring and arranging each wound separately, and adapt to what comes up, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the shoulder often breaks several times, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and its repair is this: i.e., the first step being to set the broken part above the breakage point, and the second below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the veins lie on its surface, then extend each minister's line to its equal part; and this is when the breakage occurs inside the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thumb, then one should apply the ligaments towards the knife, and the other ones over the breakage.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And similarly if it is close to the knee joint, then apply the ligaments around the knee joint, and instead of that perform extension. Then position the bone halfway between her hands, as long as it fits with her natural figure, and then place the plaster and bandage, should any abscesses not come about.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is pus to remove, let it heal first before you return to your work and treatment; the wound is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary for you to wrap around the fracture with a hard bandage doubled two or three times, leaving any excess. Then turn the leg until the heels reach the knee, and place the needle long between the foot and leg, under the knee joint from below, and guide the head of the needle above; then wrap the leg again on the thigh and the bandage, then place a pin on the fracture site, and place a pin on the bone of the leg; then position four layers of silk cloth between the leg and thigh to ensure uniform pressure, then begin to bind tightly in three or four turns around the fracture. And when you go further above the fracture and less tighten; then guide two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and thigh, and bind three pins which are on top, then return below to the head of the needle until you reach underfoot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, until no other signs come about.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, release it and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch hold, it should be removed, so long as one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to cut the wound and draw out the strength; and treat him as we have said, until he heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no part of the flesh is broken when these pins are inserted in such places, as in the shoulder and on the arm; nevertheless, no inconvenience affects the patient in this manner of restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the flesh is restored within one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the variety of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee, there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's usually just a crack, or it might be lost, causing pain in all injuries and being felt well by one.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to place it even with what was round at its ends until it's assembled and moves as it should. Then put on plaster, and add a round stick if needed, then tighten appropriately. Afterwards adjust every arrangement that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as pus formation or similar conditions; for each situation apply what suits it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Regarding the breaking of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by the right name "ham" and the other is named "foscile"; and it experiences all kinds of breakage similar to what happens in the arm, and similarly its treatment follows like for the arm equally, and the processes are all the same. And if both these bones are broken together, then the leg twists everywhere.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then twist in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and then it twists around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then adjust the position and make it even, and evenly tie the threads but always, if breakage is messy and there are several pieces, that the extension should be smaller and more gentle; and apply according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two lengths of wadded cloth that cover the leg on both sides and are long enough from the thigh down to below. Then wrap these around with two pieces of bandage above and below, and tie them in the middle as well; so that the leg does not bend either to the right or left, and thus is done properly; and no one should administer to it a single piece of cloth as long as the leg, made of wood, and place this under the leg to prevent movement. This should be carried out exactly where there is damage from the breakage or wound; and move the leg each day in order to check for pus or any other complication; treat it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the knee
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from breaking, but when bones at the knee are broken, there is a break and in the legs, powerlessness occurs in multiple positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones at the knee break, and you see these bones thrusting over one another, place these limbs of earth under your feet just as if they were going somewhere, then put now your foot on his, where the bones are elevated, press them so much until their heels revive; then set plaster and bindings over it, and put a small table at two feet thick under the belly of the knee, then restrain him to the foot insertion, then when you have wrapped cloths around him, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, repair them, as we have said about the ribs of the hand; then place a splint on the broken rib according to its length, and make it slightly wider than that. Then put under the splint the board I mentioned, and apply pressure evenly; and if there are two or three or more broken ribs, break them, placing one splint for each rib according to its size, wrapped in a single linen cloth of the first, then fix the board under the patient's abdomen where it is cut. And while lying on the table top above the patient's belly, ensure that it properly cuts through.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other matters I have discussed regarding other injuries, once we have talked about them; and correct each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural bone of the woman is broken, make her stay in an enlarged position, then incline her towards the lower back part and hold her from behind. Fill the gap that nature made with cotton, also filling it as large as possible. Then let the woman stand up slowly and lift her back bit by bit, then jump out the cotton until it comes to the entrance of natural formation, and return the bone along with her stool; and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has done so, put her back in place again, like this for seven days or more: if the breakage is healed, take a goat's bladder, tie it to the knot of the string, stuff all the bladder into natural formation, then blow into the string strongly until the bladder is inflated inside; nature will return the breakage. Then fill with cotton and let it be like this for some days, until it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand is broken, or from the woman if it is repaired as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these near breaks are not hidden by him who dedicates his study and use to this, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means in many positions the right path of restoration: thus understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oxtail and fill it with the penis; then wrap it tightly in bandages, and let it be for three days or longer, and it will heal very quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	By fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it's large, like in the case of the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, that they be surgically treated now, so that the surgeries we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, then seal it with vitriol, or if you have nothing else, then start to treat the fracture at that same hour, or on that day, assuming no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses appear, then let the treatment continue until a new day, as long as the abscess is calming down, and don't touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible at its exposed knee, then it should be put back together lightly with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not available to make it even with your hands, then you use this tool made of iron, which is seven inches or six inches long, and its width matches the size of the wound; for this task, the surgeon must adjust its size as needed for each treatment of a broken bone; it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression on your limb during surgery, and it should be sharp in front, and large at the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called 'palanché' because it requires that the crooked shoulders be placed on the tip of the visible bone; and beat it once until it heals and they are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the tools cannot properly grasp the bone, it requires that you place the tip of the bone until the tools have capability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this task, such as a scalpel or awl, with your skill; then take out what is remaining in the hard and small cuts of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels intense pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you want it to be in its natural position, then soak the dressing in a black, medicinal wine and ensure that if done correctly, especially when dealing with external injuries. Don't place anything like wax or other substances on the wound which might cause irritation; avoid causing infection and decay. Then administer herbs after you have restored the bone, keep the wound open and cover it completely according to the size of the injury, making sure to closely watch that the wound is not restricted by friction. Many people have made this mistake, leading to death or decay in the patient. And when you apply pressure gently and cautiously instead of forcefully like other breaks, these outcomes are less likely to occur; take good care that the injury doesn't heal improperly.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that harmful incidents have occurred within it, as we have said, and you find pain in your hand, then it should not be treated with stones; but encase it internally, instead of stones, bind strong cloths around it, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see that after one or two days the wound is swelling, remove whatever you have put on it with vinegar, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as the fourfold medicine and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you dislocate the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should have been so that the limb is bound in such a way that the bone slides down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it continues for the whole day, and it cannot join anymore, know that there are small fragments of bone, so you must seek to open the wound with a probe, and remove all these necessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a sinus develops in the hand or any other form of corruption, it is necessary to treat it according to what was instructed in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open within the limb, like in the elbow or shoulder, or other similar large bones, do not attempt to remove them as many times people die because of this. Leave it until it heals naturally; occasionally it might drain on its own after about 20 or 30 days. Then treat the wound if you can, and if you cannot, let it be as is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come many times after the wound has healed, especially near joints, and an ugly thing to see is the appearance of the limb; and by chance it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if there is any swelling: if you administer restorative medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, as well as sanguine collyrium, caraway, and similar others, do so with one of these things, or all together, and mix them with stinging wine, or with a whole egg or with honey; then apply this mixture on the spot in poultices, bind it tightly, and don't release it by hand for several days; then remove it, and repeat another application until the swellings are gone. Or you can apply this on a well-made piece of leather because the properties of leather have the ability to drain all swellings from the limbs; if the swelling has turned hard like stone and needs to be removed, if there is any excess, make it obvious; or continue applying it until it's reduced by any barber, until it's gone, and continue treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that becomes weak after an illness.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone has been restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to certain reasons: because one is for those who were bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and could not allow the necessary movements in the limb; or for an excess of bleeding; or for overly large movements, not at their proper time; or because they lack much blood within their body, being feeble.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you must make the patient eat the medicine, and make the body tender until the pus multiplies within him; then give him baths, and bring him joy and ease. After this, apply grease to the limb, so that the grease attracts to the large pus, and washes it often with hot water until the pus aligns with the limb; and restores its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member becomes twisted after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones break open, even though the body's natural form is lost, it does not lose its function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break all new members completely; many fools do this in our land. These practices are criticized and cause great harms, sometimes leading to death. However, when the fractures and injuries are fresh, they should be immersed in hot water or cooked with soothing herbs like dandelion leaves, roots, and milk thistle, among others. And one should apply a poultice made from these soothing substances; you take greasy figs, grind them with cinnamon, and similar medicines that alleviate heat. Then you make a greased plaster and apply it. Or you take greasy dates and grind them with nutmeg powder, and other such medicinal substances to cool down the heat. And then you make a greased poultice and apply it.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is removed the operation of rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let each body part move once an hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twists have aged and hardened, like bones, and require being treated with iron, if it is necessary to cover up to the bone, apply subtle gentle cutting at the incision; and include consideration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none, if now is needed bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	And if one delays, the limbs swell up and unexpectedly cause pain in certain parts of the body; for this reason it is not advisable to move them when they are swollen: many times pus and other pains are drawn out. However, whenever this happens, have a surgeon examine the patient, then let him rest until his abscesses subside; then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, gently apply movement, and cure each part according to how it is supposed to function within its own body.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters about shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated backward, and the dislocations of both are according to two ways: or they are slightly bone-like from their places, and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the heels, and causing saliva from the mouth that one cannot hold, nor can close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can often return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is whole and completed, you should apply the remedy quickly, without hesitation; and do so in such a way that the attendant cuts off the head of the patient and sticks the sharp end of the implement into the base of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth if the dislocation involves two parts. If only one hand's fingers are involved, they should stick out through the other hand to keep them aligned; instruct the patient that they should soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And guide her until she settles back into its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it becomes difficult to return them, even when the two jaws are together, if they were raised with hot water and oil, until you gently reset them; do not overly strain during the resetting process, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.
